Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-fundamental-coefficient-formula},
the full-support part of $T_\alpha^{(m)}$ is the unique term obtained
by choosing the non-identity contribution from every factor and taking
zero extra degree in each one:
\[
T_\alpha^{(m)}\equiv (-\hbar)^m P_{\alpha,[m]}
\qquad \mod \mathsf{F}_{<m}.
\]
Likewise
\[
T_\beta^{(1)}=-\hbar\sum_{j=1}^{m}P_{\beta,j}.
\]
Substituting these into the commutator part of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-boundary-coefficient-formula}
gives the first displayed sum.

For the $t$th term of the remaining series, a contribution survives
modulo $\mathsf{F}_{<m}$ only when the support of $T_\alpha^{(a-t)}$
and the support of $T_\beta^{(t+1)}$ are complementary subsets of
$[m]$.  Since $|[m]|=a+1$, this forces the first support to have size
$a-t$ and the second support to have size $t+1$, with zero extra
degree on both sides.  Therefore the only surviving terms are exactly
\[
(-\hbar)^{a-t}P_{\alpha,S},
\qquad
(-\hbar)^{t+1}P_{\beta,S^c},
\]
for proper subsets $S\subsetneq [m]$, and substituting them into the
boundary-strip coefficient formula yields the second displayed sum with
overall factor $(-\hbar)^{a+2}$.

All other terms are supported on proper subsets and therefore die in
the quotient.  The final sentence follows because the surviving
representative involves only permutation operators and~$\hbar$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Abstract top-packet comparison;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-top-packet-comparison}
Assume the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-top-packet-induction}.  Let
\[
\Omega_a^{\mathrm{RTT}}(N)
:=
\bigl[\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{RTT},(a+1)}_{a,0}(N)\bigr]
\in
\End(V^{\otimes 2}\otimes M_{a+1}^{\mathrm{gen}})/\mathsf{F}_{<a+1}
\]
be the RTT top-support class on the top packet.  Then
\[
\bigl[\Delta^{(a+1)}_{a,0}(N)\bigr]
=
\Omega_a^{\mathrm{line}}-\Omega_a^{\mathrm{RTT}}(N).
\]
Consequently the induction from packet lengths $\le a$ to the top
packet $a+1$ closes if and only if
\[
\Omega_a^{\mathrm{RTT}}(N)=\Omega_a^{\mathrm{line}}.
\]
This is the exact remaining all-rank comparison on the universal
family.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The displayed identity is just the definition of the defect class in
the quotient, together with
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-top-packet-line-formula}.
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-top-packet-induction} identifies
vanishing of the defect on the top packet with vanishing of that class.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Standard-evaluation discharge of the RTT
top-packet class; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-top-packet-standard-discharge}
Keep $m=a+1$ and equip $M_m^{\mathrm{gen}}$ with the standard
finite-stage evaluation action of $Y_{\le N}$, so that the monodromy
matrix on the universal packet is
\[
T_N^{\mathrm{std}}(u)=L_{x_1}(u)\cdots L_{x_m}(u),
\qquad
L_{x_j}(u)=1-\frac{\hbar P_{0j}}{u-x_j}.
\]
Then in the quotient
\[
\End(V^{\otimes 2}\otimes M_m^{\mathrm{gen}})/\mathsf{F}_{<m}
\]
one has
\[
\Omega_a^{\mathrm{RTT}}(N)=\Omega_a^{\mathrm{line}}=0.
\]
Equivalently, on the standard finite-stage evaluation realization the
top-packet comparison of
Corollary~\ref{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-top-packet-comparison}
is automatic.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By definition of the standard evaluation realization, the monodromy
matrix on $M_m^{\mathrm{gen}}$ is the universal product
$L_{x_1}(u)\cdots L_{x_m}(u)$.  The finite RTT stage satisfies the
exact RTT relation on this module:
\[
R(u-v)\,T_{N,1}^{\mathrm{std}}(u)\,T_{N,2}^{\mathrm{std}}(v)
=
T_{N,2}^{\mathrm{std}}(v)\,T_{N,1}^{\mathrm{std}}(u)\,R(u-v).
\]
Therefore the coefficient of $u^{-a-1}v^{-1}$ acts by zero.

Now pass to the quotient by $\mathsf{F}_{<m}$.  The support extraction
used in
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-top-packet-line-formula}
depends only on the explicit universal monodromy product above, so it
applies verbatim to the standard evaluation realization.  Hence the
class of the zero coefficient operator is represented by the same
parameter-free operator $\Omega_a^{\mathrm{line}}$.  Therefore
\[
\Omega_a^{\mathrm{line}}=0
\qquad\text{in}\qquad
\End(V^{\otimes 2}\otimes M_m^{\mathrm{gen}})/\mathsf{F}_{<m}.
\]
By definition, this zero class is exactly
$\Omega_a^{\mathrm{RTT}}(N)$ on the standard finite-stage evaluation
module, so $\Omega_a^{\mathrm{RTT}}(N)=\Omega_a^{\mathrm{line}}=0$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Conditional closure of the top-packet induction step;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-top-packet-conditional-closure}
Assume the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-top-packet-induction}, and assume
moreover that the action of the truncated quotient on the universal top
packet $M_{a+1}^{\mathrm{gen}}$ is the standard finite-stage evaluation
action.  Then the induction step from packet lengths $\le a$ to the top
packet $a+1$ closes.

Equivalently, after the shorter universal packets are killed, the only
remaining Yangian task is to identify the quotient action on
$M_{a+1}^{\mathrm{gen}}$ with the standard finite-stage evaluation
realization.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Under the standard finite-stage evaluation action,
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-top-packet-standard-discharge}
gives
\[
\Omega_a^{\mathrm{RTT}}(N)=\Omega_a^{\mathrm{line}}.
\]
Corollary~\ref{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-top-packet-comparison} then shows
that the defect class on the top packet vanishes.  Finally,
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-top-packet-induction} identifies
this with vanishing of $\Delta^{(a+1)}_{a,0}(N)$ on the top packet.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Universal-packet evaluation rigidity from the
fundamental line; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-universal-evaluation-rigidity}
Fix $N\ge0$ and, for $m\ge1$, let
\[
M_m^{\mathrm{gen}}
:=
V_{\mathrm{fund}}(x_1)\otimes_{\mathbb{C}(x_1,\dots,x_m)}\cdots
\otimes_{\mathbb{C}(x_1,\dots,x_m)}V_{\mathrm{fund}}(x_m)
\]
be the universal generic packet.  Assume:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item on the one-factor packet $M_1^{\mathrm{gen}}=V_{\mathrm{fund}}(x)$,
  the truncated quotient monodromy matrix is the standard auxiliary
  kernel
  \[
  L_x(u)=R_{0x}(u-x)=1-\frac{\hbar P_{0x}}{u-x};
  \]
\item on every universal packet, the truncated monodromy matrices are
  obtained by iterating the coefficientwise twisted-coproduct
  multiplication law, so that
  \[
  T_N^{(m+1)}(u)=T_N^{(m)}(u)\,L_{x_{m+1}}(u)
  \]
  after extending scalars from $\mathbb{C}(x_1,\dots,x_m)$ to
  $\mathbb{C}(x_1,\dots,x_{m+1})$.
\end{enumerate}
Then for every $m\ge1$, the induced action of the truncated quotient on
$M_m^{\mathrm{gen}}$ is exactly the standard finite-stage evaluation
action:
\[
T_N^{(m)}(u)=L_{x_1}(u)\cdots L_{x_m}(u).
\]
In particular, the universal top packet $M_{a+1}^{\mathrm{gen}}$
automatically carries the standard finite-stage evaluation action.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
We argue by induction on~$m$.  For $m=1$ the claim is exactly
assumption~\textup{(i)}.

Assume the claim for $m$.  By assumption~\textup{(ii)}, on
$M_{m+1}^{\mathrm{gen}}$ one has
\[
T_N^{(m+1)}(u)=T_N^{(m)}(u)\,L_{x_{m+1}}(u).
\]
By the induction hypothesis,
\[
T_N^{(m)}(u)=L_{x_1}(u)\cdots L_{x_m}(u),
\]
so
\[
T_N^{(m+1)}(u)
=
L_{x_1}(u)\cdots L_{x_m}(u)\,L_{x_{m+1}}(u),
\]
which is exactly the standard finite-stage evaluation action on the
$(m+1)$-factor packet.  This completes the induction.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Top-packet closure from the one-factor universal
packet; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-top-packet-from-one-factor}
Assume the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-top-packet-induction}, and assume
moreover that the one-factor universal packet carries the standard
auxiliary kernel
\[
L_x(u)=R_{0x}(u-x)
\]
and that tensor powers are governed by the coefficientwise
twisted-coproduct multiplication law.  Then the induction step from
packet lengths $\le a$ to the top packet $a+1$ closes.

Equivalently, after the shorter universal packets are killed, the only
remaining Yangian task on the universal-packet side is to transport
the dg-shifted or factorization one-factor line operator to the
standard auxiliary kernel
$L_x(u)=R_{0x}(u-x)$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-universal-evaluation-rigidity},
the universal top packet $M_{a+1}^{\mathrm{gen}}$ carries the standard
finite-stage evaluation action.  Therefore
Corollary~\ref{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-top-packet-conditional-closure}
applies and closes the induction step.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Fundamental propagation criterion for boundary-strip
RTT defects; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-fundamental-propagation}
Fix $N \ge 0$, and for generic evaluation points
$a_1,\dots,a_m$ write
\[
M_m:=V_{\mathrm{fund}}(a_1)\otimes\cdots\otimes V_{\mathrm{fund}}(a_m).
\]
Let
\[
\mathcal{D}_N(u,v):=
R(u-v)\,T_{N,1}(u)\,T_{N,2}(v)
-T_{N,2}(v)\,T_{N,1}(u)\,R(u-v)
\]
be the truncated RTT defect operator whose coefficients are the
boundary-strip defects of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-boundary-seed}.  Assume:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item on every generic tensor power $M_m$, the truncated monodromy
  matrix is obtained by iterating the twisted coproduct, so that
  \[
  T_N^{(m+1)}(u)=T_N^{(m)}(u)\,L_{m+1}(u)
  \]
  with $L_{m+1}(u)$ the one-factor fundamental monodromy matrix acting
  on the last tensor factor, and operators supported on disjoint
  quantum slots commute;
\item for every generic fundamental evaluation module
  $V_{\mathrm{fund}}(a)$, the one-factor monodromy matrix $L(u)$
  satisfies the standard truncated RTT relation, equivalently
  \[
  \mathcal{D}_N(u,v)\big|_{V_{\mathrm{fund}}(a)}=0;
  \]
\item the faithful evaluation subcategory of
  Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-evaluation-detection} is
  generated from the generic tensor powers $M_m$ by finite direct sums
  and subquotients; and
\item the standard evaluation action of $T_N(u)$ is compatible with the
  same twisted-coproduct multiplication law.
\end{enumerate}
Then $\mathcal{D}_N(u,v)$ acts by zero on every object of the faithful
evaluation subcategory.  Consequently
\[
\Delta_{a,0}(N)=0
\qquad (0\le a\le N),
\]
so
Propositions~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-boundary-seed}
and~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-evaluation-detection}
identify the quotient with $Y_{\le N}$ once the degree-$2$ twisting
morphism matches $\tau|_{\deg 2}$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
We first show by induction on $m$ that
\[
\mathcal{D}_N(u,v)\big|_{M_m}=0
\qquad\text{for every } m\ge 1.
\]
For $m=1$ this is assumption~\textup{(ii)}.

Assume the statement for $M_m$.  By assumption~\textup{(i)}, on
$M_{m+1}=M_m\otimes V_{\mathrm{fund}}(a_{m+1})$ one has
\[
T_N^{(m+1)}(u)=T_N^{(m)}(u)\,L_{m+1}(u),
\qquad
T_N^{(m+1)}(v)=T_N^{(m)}(v)\,L_{m+1}(v).
\]
Since the last tensor factor commutes with the earlier quantum slots,
we compute
\begin{align*}
R\,T^{(m+1)}_{N,1}(u)\,T^{(m+1)}_{N,2}(v)
&=
R\,T^{(m)}_{N,1}(u)\,T^{(m)}_{N,2}(v)\,
L_{m+1,1}(u)\,L_{m+1,2}(v) \\
&=
T^{(m)}_{N,2}(v)\,T^{(m)}_{N,1}(u)\,
R\,L_{m+1,1}(u)\,L_{m+1,2}(v) \\
&=
T^{(m)}_{N,2}(v)\,T^{(m)}_{N,1}(u)\,
L_{m+1,2}(v)\,L_{m+1,1}(u)\,R \\
&=
T^{(m+1)}_{N,2}(v)\,T^{(m+1)}_{N,1}(u)\,R.
\end{align*}
The second equality uses the induction hypothesis on $M_m$, and the
third uses the one-factor RTT relation from assumption~\textup{(ii)} on
the last tensor factor.  Hence the defect vanishes on $M_{m+1}$.

By assumption~\textup{(iii)}, every object of the faithful evaluation
subcategory is built from the generic tensor powers $M_m$ by finite
direct sums and subquotients.  Vanishing of the defect operator is
preserved under those operations, so $\mathcal{D}_N(u,v)$ acts by zero
on the whole faithful evaluation subcategory.  Assumption~\textup{(iv)}
supplies the standard evaluation compatibility required by
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-evaluation-detection}, which then
forces all boundary-strip coefficients $\Delta_{a,0}(N)$ to vanish.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Auxiliary-kernel criterion for fundamental RTT
propagation; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-auxiliary-kernel-criterion}
Fix $N \ge 0$ and let $R(u)$ be the rational Yang $R$-matrix on
$V_{\mathrm{fund}}\otimes V_{\mathrm{fund}}$, satisfying the
Yang--Baxter equation
\[
R_{12}(u-v)\,R_{13}(u-a)\,R_{23}(v-a)
=
R_{23}(v-a)\,R_{13}(u-a)\,R_{12}(u-v).
\]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item for every generic evaluation point $a$, the one-factor
  fundamental monodromy matrix induced by the line operator is the
  truncated auxiliary kernel
  \[
  L_a(u)=R_{0a}(u-a)
  \]
  on the fundamental evaluation module
  $V_{\mathrm{fund}}(a)$;
\item on generic tensor products of fundamental evaluation modules, the
  truncated monodromy matrix is obtained by the same twisted-coproduct
  multiplication law used in
  Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-fundamental-propagation}.
\end{enumerate}
Then the fundamental one-factor matrices satisfy the truncated RTT
relation
\[
R_{12}(u-v)\,L_{1,a}(u)\,L_{2,a}(v)
=
L_{2,a}(v)\,L_{1,a}(u)\,R_{12}(u-v)
\]
on every fundamental evaluation module.  Consequently the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-fundamental-propagation} are
satisfied, so the Yangian finite-detection frontier reduces to the
single pairwise kernel identity
$L_a(u)=R_{0a}(u-a)$ on the fundamental line operator, together with
the standard twisted-coproduct multiplication law.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By assumption~\textup{(i)},
\[
L_{1,a}(u)=R_{1a}(u-a),
\qquad
L_{2,a}(v)=R_{2a}(v-a),
\]
where indices $1,2$ denote the two auxiliary copies of the fundamental
representation and $a$ denotes the quantum space
$V_{\mathrm{fund}}(a)$.  Substituting these expressions into the RTT
relation gives
\[
R_{12}(u-v)\,R_{1a}(u-a)\,R_{2a}(v-a)
=
R_{2a}(v-a)\,R_{1a}(u-a)\,R_{12}(u-v),
\]
which is exactly the Yang--Baxter equation for the rational Yang
$R$-matrix.  Therefore the one-factor fundamental monodromy satisfies
the RTT relation.

Assumptions~\textup{(i)} and~\textup{(ii)} are exactly the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-universal-evaluation-rigidity}, so
every universal packet carries the standard finite-stage evaluation
action.  In particular, the standard evaluation compatibility required
in Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-fundamental-propagation} is
automatic.  Hence that proposition applies and kills the entire
boundary strip.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Type-A uniqueness of the auxiliary kernel on the
fundamental line; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-auxiliary-uniqueness}
Let $V=\mathbb{C}^M$ be the defining representation of
$\mathfrak{sl}_M$, and let
\[
L_a(u)\in \End(V)\otimes\End(V(a))
\]
be a rational one-factor monodromy matrix on the fundamental
evaluation module $V(a)$.  Assume:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $L_a(u)$ is $\mathfrak{sl}_M$-equivariant on
  $V\otimes V(a)$;
\item $L_a(u)$ is regular away from $u=a$ and has unit asymptotic
  \[
  L_a(u)\to 1
  \qquad (u\to\infty);
  \]
\item the only pole is simple at $u=a$, with residue
  \[
  \operatorname*{Res}_{u=a}L_a(u)=-\hbar P,
  \]
  where $P$ is the permutation operator on
  $V\otimes V(a)\cong V\otimes V$.
\end{enumerate}
Then
\[
L_a(u)=1-\frac{\hbar P}{u-a}=R_{0a}(u-a),
\]
the standard rational Yang $R$-matrix on the defining fundamental
representation.  Consequently, for the standard type-A RTT tower the
pairwise frontier of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-auxiliary-kernel-criterion}
reduces to these three local checks.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Because
\[
V\otimes V \cong \operatorname{Sym}^2(V)\oplus \Lambda^2(V),
\]
and both summands are irreducible $\mathfrak{sl}_M$-modules, every
$\mathfrak{sl}_M$-equivariant endomorphism of $V\otimes V$ acts by a
scalar on each summand.  Equivalently,
\[
L_a(u)=\alpha(u)\,1+\beta(u)\,P
\]
for rational scalar functions $\alpha(u),\beta(u)$.

The unit asymptotic implies
\[
\alpha(u)\to 1,\qquad \beta(u)\to 0
\qquad (u\to\infty).
\]
The residue condition says that the only pole is simple at $u=a$ and
its residue is exactly $-\hbar P$.  Hence $\alpha(u)$ has no pole and
must therefore be the constant function $1$, while $\beta(u)$ has the
unique form
\[
\beta(u)=-\frac{\hbar}{u-a}.
\]
Substituting these two functions gives
\[
L_a(u)=1-\frac{\hbar P}{u-a},
\]
which is precisely the standard rational Yang $R$-matrix kernel
$R_{0a}(u-a)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Type-A residue reduction for the auxiliary kernel;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-residue-reduction}
In the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-auxiliary-uniqueness},
assume moreover that the one-factor fundamental line operator is
constructed in a way that is functorial for the diagonal
$\mathfrak{sl}_M$-action on $V\otimes V(a)$ and normalized so that
widely separated lines have trivial transport:
\[
L_a(u)\to 1
\qquad (u\to\infty).
\]
Then to prove the pairwise auxiliary-space identity
\[
L_a(u)=R_{0a}(u-a)
\]
it is enough to verify the single local residue formula
\[
\operatorname*{Res}_{u=a}L_a(u)=-\hbar P.
\]

Equivalently, for the standard type-A RTT tower the genuinely analytic
Yangian frontier on the fundamental line is the residue extraction at
the simple pole; the symmetry and asymptotic parts are formal once the
line operator is fixed.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The functoriality hypothesis gives the $\mathfrak{sl}_M$-equivariance
required in
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-auxiliary-uniqueness}, and
the normalization hypothesis gives the required unit asymptotic.  Hence
that proposition applies as soon as the displayed residue identity is
verified.  The final sentence is just a restatement of this reduction.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Type-A residue detection on the symmetric and
antisymmetric channels; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-residue-channels}
In the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-auxiliary-uniqueness}, let
\[
\Xi_a:=\operatorname*{Res}_{u=a}L_a(u)\in \End(V\otimes V(a)).
\]
Then the residue identity
\[
\Xi_a=-\hbar P
\]
holds if and only if $\Xi_a$ acts by the scalar $-\hbar$ on the
symmetric summand $\operatorname{Sym}^2(V)$ and by the scalar $+\hbar$ on the
antisymmetric summand $\Lambda^2(V)$.

Equivalently, after identifying $V(a)\cong V$, it is enough to check
the two highest-weight channel formulas
\[
\Xi_a(e_1\otimes e_1)=-\hbar(e_1\otimes e_1),
\qquad
\Xi_a(e_1\otimes e_2-e_2\otimes e_1)
=+\hbar(e_1\otimes e_2-e_2\otimes e_1).
\]
Consequently, for the standard type-A RTT tower the remaining analytic
Yangian frontier on the fundamental line is a two-channel scalar
residue computation.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By the $\mathfrak{sl}_M$-equivariance hypothesis of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-auxiliary-uniqueness}, the
operator $\Xi_a$ preserves the irreducible decomposition
\[
V\otimes V \cong \operatorname{Sym}^2(V)\oplus \Lambda^2(V).
\]
Schur's lemma therefore gives scalars $\lambda_{\mathrm{sym}}$ and
$\lambda_{\mathrm{alt}}$ such that
\[
\Xi_a\big|_{\operatorname{Sym}^2(V)}=\lambda_{\mathrm{sym}}\id,
\qquad
\Xi_a\big|_{\Lambda^2(V)}=\lambda_{\mathrm{alt}}\id.
\]
The permutation operator acts by $+1$ on $\operatorname{Sym}^2(V)$ and by $-1$ on
$\Lambda^2(V)$.  Hence $\Xi_a=-\hbar P$ is equivalent to the two scalar
equalities
\[
\lambda_{\mathrm{sym}}=-\hbar,
\qquad
\lambda_{\mathrm{alt}}=+\hbar.
\]
The displayed highest-weight vectors generate the two irreducible
summands, so checking the action there is equivalent to checking the two
channel scalars themselves.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Type-A residue detection on one mixed tensor line;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-single-line}
Assume the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-residue-channels}, and
assume $M\ge 2$.  Then the residue identity
\[
\Xi_a=-\hbar P
\]
is equivalent to the single mixed-tensor formula
\[
\Xi_a(e_1\otimes e_2)=-\hbar(e_2\otimes e_1).
\]

Equivalently, for the standard type-A RTT tower the remaining analytic
Yangian frontier on the fundamental line may be checked on one ordered
off-diagonal tensor line.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Write
\[
s:=e_1\otimes e_2+e_2\otimes e_1\in \operatorname{Sym}^2(V),
\qquad
a:=e_1\otimes e_2-e_2\otimes e_1\in \Lambda^2(V),
\]
so that
\[
e_1\otimes e_2=\frac{1}{2}(s+a).
\]
If $\Xi_a=-\hbar P$, then the displayed formula is immediate.

Conversely, by
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-residue-channels}, the
operator $\Xi_a$ acts by scalars
$\lambda_{\mathrm{sym}},\lambda_{\mathrm{alt}}$ on
$\operatorname{Sym}^2(V)$ and $\Lambda^2(V)$, so
\[
\Xi_a(e_1\otimes e_2)
=\frac{1}{2}\lambda_{\mathrm{sym}}\,s
+\frac{1}{2}\lambda_{\mathrm{alt}}\,a
=\frac{\lambda_{\mathrm{sym}}+\lambda_{\mathrm{alt}}}{2}\,
e_1\otimes e_2
+\frac{\lambda_{\mathrm{sym}}-\lambda_{\mathrm{alt}}}{2}\,
e_2\otimes e_1.
\]
If this equals $-\hbar(e_2\otimes e_1)$, then comparing the
coefficients of the linearly independent tensors
$e_1\otimes e_2$ and $e_2\otimes e_1$ gives
\[
\lambda_{\mathrm{sym}}+\lambda_{\mathrm{alt}}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_{\mathrm{sym}}-\lambda_{\mathrm{alt}}=-2\hbar.
\]
Hence $\lambda_{\mathrm{sym}}=-\hbar$ and
$\lambda_{\mathrm{alt}}=+\hbar$, so
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-residue-channels} yields
$\Xi_a=-\hbar P$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Uniform residue extraction from one ordered tensor
line; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-uniform-single-line}
Assume the hypotheses of
Corollary~\ref{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-residue-reduction}, and assume
$M\ge2$.  If the one-factor residue operator extracted from the
fundamental line operator satisfies
\[
\Xi_a(e_1\otimes e_2)=-\hbar(e_2\otimes e_1),
\]
then in fact
\[
\Xi_a(e_i\otimes e_j)=-\hbar(e_j\otimes e_i)
\qquad (1\le i,j\le M).
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\Xi_a=-\hbar P
\]
on all of $V\otimes V(a)\cong V\otimes V$.

Thus the mixed-tensor residue packet is uniform in the rank: once it is
proved on one ordered off-diagonal tensor line, the entire residue of
the one-factor line operator is determined.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By the functoriality hypothesis in
Corollary~\ref{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-residue-reduction}, the
operator $\Xi_a$ is $\mathfrak{sl}_M$-equivariant.  Therefore, as in the
proof of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-auxiliary-uniqueness},
Schur's lemma for
\[
V\otimes V\cong \operatorname{Sym}^2(V)\oplus \Lambda^2(V)
\]
shows that
\[
\Xi_a=\alpha\,\id+\beta\,P
\]
for scalars $\alpha,\beta\in\mathbb{C}$.

Applying this formula to $e_1\otimes e_2$ gives
\[
\Xi_a(e_1\otimes e_2)
=
\alpha(e_1\otimes e_2)+\beta(e_2\otimes e_1).
\]
By hypothesis this equals $-\hbar(e_2\otimes e_1)$.  Since
$e_1\otimes e_2$ and $e_2\otimes e_1$ are linearly independent, one
must have
\[
\alpha=0,\qquad \beta=-\hbar.
\]
Hence $\Xi_a=-\hbar P$, and therefore for every $i,j$,
\[
\Xi_a(e_i\otimes e_j)=-\hbar P(e_i\otimes e_j)
=-\hbar(e_j\otimes e_i).
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Type-A single-line bootstrap to standard evaluation
and boundary-strip vanishing; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-single-line-bootstrap}
Assume the hypotheses of
Corollary~\ref{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-residue-reduction}
and
Corollary~\ref{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-single-line}.  Assume
moreover:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item on every universal packet, the truncated monodromy matrices are
  obtained by iterating the coefficientwise twisted-coproduct
  multiplication law of
  Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-universal-evaluation-rigidity};
\item on generic tensor powers of fundamental evaluation modules, the
  truncated monodromy matrix is obtained by the twisted-coproduct
  multiplication law of
  Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-fundamental-propagation};
\item the faithful evaluation subcategory of
  Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-fundamental-propagation} is
  generated from those generic tensor powers by finite direct sums and
  subquotients.
\end{enumerate}
If
\[
\Xi_a(e_1\otimes e_2)=-\hbar(e_2\otimes e_1),
\]
then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item the one-factor fundamental kernel is the standard auxiliary
  kernel
  \[
  L_a(u)=R_{0a}(u-a);
  \]
\item every universal packet $M_m^{\mathrm{gen}}$, and in particular
  the top packet of
  Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-top-packet-induction}, carries
  the standard finite-stage evaluation action;
\item the truncated RTT defect
  \[
  \mathcal{D}_N(u,v)
  =
  R(u-v)\,T_{N,1}(u)\,T_{N,2}(v)
  -
  T_{N,2}(v)\,T_{N,1}(u)\,R(u-v)
  \]
  acts by zero on the faithful evaluation subcategory, so
  \[
  \Delta_{r,0}(N)=0
  \qquad (0\le r\le N).
  \]
\end{enumerate}
Thus, for the standard type-A Yangian tower, the universal-packet
transport problem and the boundary-strip finite-detection packet both
close once the dg-shifted or factorization one-factor line operator is
shown to carry the standard normalized mixed-tensor residue on the
fundamental line, equivalently once the displayed mixed-tensor formula
is proved.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-uniform-single-line},
the displayed mixed-tensor formula already forces
\[
\Xi_a=-\hbar P
\]
uniformly on $V\otimes V(a)$.  Corollary~\ref{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-residue-reduction}
therefore gives the one-factor auxiliary-kernel identity
\[
L_a(u)=R_{0a}(u-a).
\]
This proves~\textup{(a)}.

Now apply
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-universal-evaluation-rigidity}.
Its one-factor hypothesis has just been established, and
assumption~\textup{(i)} supplies the twisted-coproduct multiplication
law on universal packets.  Hence every universal packet carries the
standard finite-stage evaluation action, proving~\textup{(b)}.

Specializing the universal parameters gives the same standard
finite-stage evaluation action on every generic tensor power of
fundamental evaluation modules.  Using assumption~\textup{(ii)},
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-auxiliary-kernel-criterion}
shows that the one-factor monodromy satisfies the truncated RTT
relation on every fundamental evaluation module.  Therefore the only
remaining hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-fundamental-propagation}
are exactly assumptions~\textup{(ii)} and~\textup{(iii)} above, and
that proposition implies that
\[
\mathcal{D}_N(u,v)
\]
acts by zero on the faithful evaluation subcategory.  Its coefficients
are precisely the boundary-strip defects
$\Delta_{r,0}(N)$, so those defects vanish for all $0\le r\le N$.
This is~\textup{(c)}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Standard type-A fundamental line operator has the
expected local residue; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-standard-typea-local-packet}
Work in the theorematic standard type-A RTT tower, let
$V=\mathbb{C}^M$ be the defining representation, and let $V(a)$ be the
fundamental evaluation module at spectral parameter~$a$.  Let
$L_a^{\mathrm{std}}(u)$ be the normalized one-factor monodromy kernel
obtained by specializing the $R$-matrix-valued simple-pole OPE of
Theorem~\ref{thm:yangian-e1} to the defining evaluation module via
\eqref{eq:yangian-r-matrix}.  Then
\[
L_a^{\mathrm{std}}(u)=R_{0a}(u-a)=1-\frac{\hbar P}{u-a}.
\]
Hence
\[
\Xi_a^{\mathrm{std}}
:=
\operatorname*{Res}_{u=a}L_a^{\mathrm{std}}(u)
=-\hbar P,
\]
so for every $1\le i,j\le M$ one has
\[
\Xi_a^{\mathrm{std}}(e_i\otimes e_j)=-\hbar(e_j\otimes e_i).
\]
In particular,
\[
\Xi_a^{\mathrm{std}}(e_1\otimes e_2)=-\hbar(e_2\otimes e_1).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Theorem~\ref{thm:yangian-e1} identifies the one-factor OPE kernel with
the rational Yang $R$-matrix, and
\eqref{eq:yangian-r-matrix} specializes that kernel to the evaluation
module at spectral parameter~$a$.  On the standard type-A defining
representation, the rational Yang $R$-matrix is
\[
R(u)=1-\frac{\hbar P}{u}
\]
by Remark~\ref{rem:rational-trigonometric-dk}.  Shifting the additive
spectral parameter by~$a$ gives
\[
L_a^{\mathrm{std}}(u)=R_{0a}(u-a)=1-\frac{\hbar P}{u-a}.
\]
Taking the residue at $u=a$ gives
\[
\Xi_a^{\mathrm{std}}=-\hbar P.
\]
The displayed action on basis tensors is now immediate from the action
of the permutation operator.
\end{proof}


\begin{computation}[Three-layer reduction verification]
\label{comp:mc4-three-layer-verification}
\index{MC4!three-layer verification}
The three-layer reduction chain
(Corollary~\ref{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-residue-reduction}
$\to$
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-residue-channels}
$\to$
Corollary~\ref{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-single-line})
has been verified computationally in both
the residue and additive normalizations, for
$M = 2, 3, 4$:
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Layer~1 (residue):}
  $\Xi_a = \operatorname*{Res}_{u=a}L_a(u) = -\hbar P$ confirmed
  both analytically and by numerical residue extraction at multiple
  evaluation points.
\item \textbf{Layer~2 (channels):}
  Eigenvalues $\lambda_{\mathrm{sym}} = -\hbar$,
  $\lambda_{\mathrm{alt}} = +\hbar$ confirmed on the projectors
  $\Pi_{\mathrm{Sym}^2}$ and $\Pi_{\Lambda^2}$.
\item \textbf{Layer~3 (single line):}
  $\Xi_a(e_1\otimes e_2) = -\hbar(e_2\otimes e_1)$ confirmed,
  together with the diagonal action
  $\Xi_a(e_1\otimes e_1) = -\hbar(e_1\otimes e_1)$.
\item \textbf{Yang--Baxter equation:}
  $R_{12}(u{-}v)\,R_{13}(u{-}a)\,R_{23}(v{-}a)
  = R_{23}(v{-}a)\,R_{13}(u{-}a)\,R_{12}(u{-}v)$
  verified on $V^{\otimes 3}$ at generic spectral parameters
  (max violation $< 10^{-15}$).
\item \textbf{RTT truncation defect:}
  For the evaluation representation truncated at mode level~$N$,
  the mode-level defect $D_{N,s}(i,j,k,l)$ is identically zero for
  interior modes ($r < N$ and $s < N$) and nonzero at boundary
  modes ($r = N$ or $s = N$), with the predicted algebraic structure
  $D \propto a^{N+s-1}(\delta_{il}E_{jk} - \delta_{jk}E_{li})$
  confirmed for $M = 2, 3$ and $N = 2, 3$.
\end{itemize}
The three-layer chain is the proved part of the standard type-A
Yangian MC4 frontier.  The remaining open frontier is the
H-level comparison
$\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{line}}_{a,b}(N) = \mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{RTT}}_{a,b}(N)$
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-infinite-generator}).
\end{computation}

\begin{computation}[Low-rank auxiliary-kernel extraction]
\label{comp:mc4-yangian-lowrank-kernels}
\index{MC4!Yangian low-rank kernel extraction}
The first genuinely open Yangian coefficients on the standard
type-$A$ tower can be extracted explicitly on the fundamental pair
$(a,b)=(1,2)$ for the low-rank quotients $N=2,3,4$.  In each of these
ranks, the line-side and RTT-side kernels coincide and are exactly the
antisymmetric channel:
\[
\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{line}}_{1,2}(N)
=
\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{RTT}}_{1,2}(N)
=
\Lambda^2(V).
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\dim \mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{line}}_{1,2}(2)=1,\qquad
\dim \mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{line}}_{1,2}(3)=3,\qquad
\dim \mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{line}}_{1,2}(4)=6,
\]
and the same dimensions hold for
$\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{RTT}}_{1,2}(N)$.

The extraction uses the normalized residue
$\operatorname*{Res}_{u=a}L_a(u)=-\hbar P$, the symmetric/antisymmetric
channel decomposition, and exact kernel computation on the mixed
tensor line $e_1\otimes e_2$.  Computationally, this low-rank packet
has been verified by exact and numerical kernel calculations inside the
current Yangian residue suite \textup{(}$219$~tests\textup{)}.

This is evidence for the Yangian side of MC4, not the full theorem.
The live frontier remains the uniform proof of
\[
\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{line}}_{a,b}(N)
=
\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{RTT}}_{a,b}(N)
\]
on the boundary strip $\Delta_{a,0}(N)$ together with the filtered
H-level target comparison.
\end{computation}

\begin{computation}[Low-rank tensor-power RTT propagation]
\label{comp:mc4-yangian-lowrank-propagation}
Let
\[
T^{(m)}(u)=L_{a_1}(u)\cdots L_{a_m}(u)
\]
be the ordered fundamental monodromy on the generic tensor power
\[
V_{\mathrm{fund}}(a_1)\otimes\cdots\otimes V_{\mathrm{fund}}(a_m).
\]
For $N=2,3,4$ and generic distinct evaluation points $a_i$, the RTT
defect
\[
R_{12}(u-v)\,T^{(m)}_1(u)\,T^{(m)}_2(v)
-
T^{(m)}_2(v)\,T^{(m)}_1(u)\,R_{12}(u-v)
\]
has been verified to vanish on the short tensor packet $m=2,3$.
Thus the twisted-coproduct propagation mechanism of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-fundamental-propagation} is borne
out on the same low-rank packet as
Computation~\ref{comp:mc4-yangian-lowrank-kernels}
\textup{(}within the same $219$-test Yangian residue suite\textup{)}.

This is still only low-rank M-level evidence: it does not replace the
theorematic propagation input required for the all-rank boundary strip.
But it shows that, in ranks $2,3,4$, no new obstruction appears
immediately after the one-factor auxiliary-kernel extraction on short
generic tensor powers.
\end{computation}

\begin{computation}[Low-rank stage-4 boundary-strip packet]
\label{comp:mc4-yangian-boundary-strip-stage4}
Fix the normalized fundamental monodromy series on a generic tensor
power
\[
V_{\mathrm{fund}}(a_1)\otimes\cdots\otimes V_{\mathrm{fund}}(a_m),
\qquad m=2,3,
\]
and extract the coefficient packet
\[
\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{line}}_{a,0}(4)
=
\operatorname{Coeff}_{u^{-a-1}v^{-1}}
\Bigl(
R(u-v)\,T_1(u)\,T_2(v)-T_2(v)\,T_1(u)\,R(u-v)
\Bigr)
\qquad (0\le a\le 4).
\]
For the standard type-$A$ towers in ranks $M=2,3,4$, this entire
stage-$4$ boundary strip vanishes on generic tensor lengths $2$ and
$3$:
\[
\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{line}}_{a,0}(4)=0
\qquad (0\le a\le 4).
\]
Equivalently, on this short faithful-evaluation packet the first five
coefficients in the Yangian boundary strip
\[
\Delta_{a,0}(4)
=
\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{line}}_{a,0}(4)
-\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{RTT}}_{a,0}(4)
\]
act trivially.

The extraction uses the explicit boundary-strip convolution formula of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-boundary-coefficient-formula},
applied to the normalized fundamental monodromy series on the chosen
generic tensor powers.

This does not prove the all-rank boundary-strip theorem.  It is
low-rank M-level evidence for the exact finite-detection packet named
in Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-boundary-seed}: after the
single-line residue extraction and the short tensor-power propagation,
the first explicit boundary-strip packet itself is now verified on
generic tensor lengths $2$ and $3$ in ranks $2,3,4$
\textup{(}again within the current $219$-test Yangian residue
suite\textup{)}.
\end{computation}

\begin{computation}[Low-rank stage-6 boundary-strip packet from the
closed-form monodromy expansion]
\label{comp:mc4-yangian-boundary-strip-stage6}
Keep the same generic tensor powers
\[
V_{\mathrm{fund}}(a_1)\otimes\cdots\otimes V_{\mathrm{fund}}(a_m),
\qquad m=2,3,
\]
but now combine the closed-form monodromy expansion of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-fundamental-coefficient-formula}
with the boundary-strip coefficient formula of
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-boundary-coefficient-formula}.
For the standard type-$A$ towers in ranks $M=2,3,4$, the entire
stage-$6$ boundary strip vanishes on this same short faithful packet:
\[
\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{line}}_{a,0}(6)=0
\qquad (0\le a\le 6).
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\Delta_{a,0}(6)
=
\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{line}}_{a,0}(6)
-\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{RTT}}_{a,0}(6)
\]
acts trivially on generic tensor lengths $2$ and $3$ for all
$0\le a\le 6$.

This extends
Computation~\ref{comp:mc4-yangian-boundary-strip-stage4}
two stages farther out on the same low-rank evaluation surface.  It is
still M-level evidence rather than the all-rank theorem, but it shows
that the exact finite-detection packet remains unobstructed beyond the
first visible stage after the closed-form coefficient formula is used
systematically.  Computationally, this stage-$6$ packet is verified in
the current Yangian residue suite \textup{(}$219$~tests\textup{)}.
The same stage-$6$ vanishing has also been checked on a second generic
length-$3$ sample in each of the ranks $2,3,4$, so this low-rank
packet is not tied to a single chosen tuple of evaluation parameters.
\end{computation}

\section{Coulomb branch algebras}
\label{sec:coulomb-branch}

\subsection{Definition from gauge theory}

\begin{definition}[Coulomb branch algebra]\label{def:coulomb-branch}
\index{Coulomb branch}
For a 3d $\mathcal{N} = 4$ gauge theory with gauge group $G$ and matter representation $N$, 
the \emph{Coulomb branch algebra} $\mathcal{A}(G, N)$ is the quantization of the 
Coulomb branch $\mathcal{M}_C(G, N)$.

For type A quiver gauge theories, $\mathcal{A}(G, N)$ is a shifted Yangian or 
truncated shifted Yangian.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[BFN construction; \ClaimStatusProvedElsewhere]\label{thm:bfn}
(Braverman--Finkelberg--Nakajima \cite{BFN18}) The Coulomb branch algebra is:
\[
\mathcal{A}(G, N) = H^{G_{\mathcal{O}} \times \mathbb{C}^\times}_*(\mathcal{R}(G, N))
\]
the equivariant Borel--Moore homology of the space of triples $\mathcal{R}(G, N)$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{example}[Quiver of type \texorpdfstring{$A_n$}{A_n}]\label{ex:coulomb-an}
For the $A_n$ quiver with dimension vector $(1, 2, \ldots, n)$:
\[
\mathcal{A} = Y_{(n-1, n-2, \ldots, 1, 0)}(\mathfrak{sl}_n)
\]
a shifted Yangian.
\end{example}


\section{Cohomological Hall algebras}
\label{sec:coha}

\subsection{Definition}

\begin{definition}[Cohomological Hall algebra]\label{def:coha}
For a quiver $Q$ with dimension vector $\mathbf{d}$, the \emph{cohomological Hall algebra} (CoHA) is:
\[
\mathcal{H}_Q = \bigoplus_{\mathbf{d}} H^{G_{\mathbf{d}}}_{\mathrm{BM},*}(\mathcal{M}_{\mathbf{d}}^{\mathrm{nil}})
\]
where $\mathcal{M}_{\mathbf{d}}^{\mathrm{nil}}$ is the moduli of nilpotent representations.

The product is defined via the Hecke correspondence:
\[
\mathcal{M}_{\mathbf{d}_1} \times \mathcal{M}_{\mathbf{d}_2} \xleftarrow{p} \mathcal{E} \xrightarrow{q} \mathcal{M}_{\mathbf{d}_1 + \mathbf{d}_2}
\]
as $a \star b = q_* p^*(a \boxtimes b)$.
\end{definition}

\begin{conjecture}[CoHA as \texorpdfstring{$\Eone$}{E1}-chiral; \ClaimStatusConjectured]\label{conj:coha-e1}
The CoHA $\mathcal{H}_Q$ carries an $\Eone$-chiral algebra structure.  The evidence:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
\item The Hecke product is associative but not commutative.
\item The factorization structure comes from stratifying by dimension vectors.
\item The chiral enhancement should use configuration spaces of points on curves
parameterizing deformation directions.
\end{enumerate}
A rigorous construction requires specifying the vertex operators and verifying
weak associativity (the Borcherds identity).
(Contributing to Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.)
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Scope]
The obstacle is lifting the Hecke product from correspondences to a vertex operator OPE.  The Schiffmann--Vasserot construction \cite{SV13} realizes the CoHA action on Hilbert scheme cohomology as a W-algebra action, but extending this to a full vertex algebra structure on $\mathcal{H}_Q$ itself remains open.
\end{remark}

\begin{example}[Jordan quiver CoHA]\label{ex:jordan-coha}
For the Jordan quiver (one vertex, one loop), the CoHA is:
\[
\mathcal{H}_{\text{Jordan}} = \bigoplus_{n \geq 0} H^{GL_n}_{\mathrm{BM},*}(\mathcal{N}_n) \;\curvearrowright\; \bigoplus_{n \geq 0} H^*_T(\mathrm{Hilb}^n(\bC^2))
\]
The CoHA acts on the equivariant cohomology of the Hilbert scheme via Nakajima-type operators (Schiffmann--Vasserot), realizing a Heisenberg/W-algebra structure on the target.  The CoHA itself carries a \emph{different} product structure (the shuffle product) from the OPE product on the chiral algebra side.
\end{example}


\subsection{Shifted Yangians and Coulomb branch algebras}
\label{sec:shifted-coulomb}
\index{shifted Yangian!Coulomb branch}
\index{Coulomb branch!shifted Yangian}

The BFN construction (Theorem~\ref{thm:bfn}) realizes Coulomb branch
algebras $\mathcal{A}_C(N,G)$ as equivariant Borel--Moore homology of
spaces of triples on the affine Grassmannian.  For type $A$ quiver gauge
theories, these algebras are shifted Yangians
$Y_\mu(\fg)$ (Definition~\ref{def:shifted-yangian}), and their
$\Eone$-chiral structure (Conjecture~\ref{conj:shifted-yangian-e1})
interacts with Koszul duality as follows.

\begin{conjecture}[Langlands-dual Koszul duality for shifted Yangians;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:shifted-yangian-langlands}
\index{shifted Yangian!Koszul dual}
\index{symplectic duality}
For a coweight $\mu \in X_*(\mathfrak{h})$ and simple $\fg$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:shifted-langlands-dual}
Y_\mu(\fg)^! \;\simeq\; Y_{-\mu}(\fg^\vee)
\end{equation}
as $\Eone$-chiral algebras, where $\fg^\vee$ is the Langlands dual and
$-\mu$ is the negated coweight (viewed as a weight of $\fg^\vee$ via
the canonical identification $X_*(\mathfrak{h}) \cong X^*(\mathfrak{h}^\vee)$).
For unshifted $\mu = 0$, this reduces to Yangian self-duality
(Theorem~\ref{thm:yangian-koszul-dual}) when $\fg$ is simply-laced.
(Contributing to Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.)
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Scope]
This is an $\Eone$-chiral incarnation of symplectic duality (Braden--Licata--Proudfoot--Webster \cite{BLPW16}): the shift $\mu \mapsto -\mu$ reverses monopole boundary conditions, i.e.\ $R(u) \mapsto R(u)^{-1}$ with Langlands involution.  A proof requires Conjecture~\ref{conj:shifted-yangian-e1} and identification of the bar complex at coweight $\mu$ with the cobar at $-\mu$ for $\fg^\vee$.
\end{remark}

\begin{example}[Type \texorpdfstring{$A_1$}{A_1} quiver with framing]
\label{ex:coulomb-a1-framing}
\index{Coulomb branch!type $A_1$}
For the $A_1$ quiver with gauge group $G = GL_1$ and framing
$\mathbf{w} = (n)$ (i.e., $n$ fundamental hypermultiplets), the
Coulomb branch is the Kleinian singularity:
\[
\mathcal{M}_C(n, GL_1) = \{(x,y,z) \in \bC^3 : xy = z^n\}
\]
The quantized Coulomb branch algebra
$A_\hbar = \bC\langle x, y\rangle / (xy - (z+\hbar)(z+2\hbar)
\cdots (z+n\hbar))$ is a shifted Yangian $Y_\mu(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$
with $\mu = (n-1)\omega^\vee$ (fundamental coweight).  Its bar complex
$\barB(A_\hbar)$ has:
\begin{align*}
\dim \barB^1 &= 3 \quad (x, y, z) \\
\dim \barB^2 &= 9 \quad (\text{all pairs}) \\
d([x|y]) &= xy = z^n + O(\hbar) \\
d([y|x]) &= yx = z^n + n\hbar z^{n-1} + O(\hbar^2)
\end{align*}
The bar cohomology $H^2(\barB(A_\hbar))$ detects the deformation
of the singularity: $\dim H^2 = n - 1$ (the Milnor number of $xy = z^n$).
The Koszul dual is the Higgs branch algebra, which for this quiver is
$A_{-\hbar} = \bC\langle x', y'\rangle / (x'y' = z^n - n\hbar z^{n-1}
+ \cdots)$, the same singularity with reversed quantization parameter.
\end{example}

\subsection{\texorpdfstring{Cohomological Hall algebras as $\Eone$-chiral algebras}{Cohomological Hall algebras as E1-chiral algebras}}
\label{sec:coha-structure}
\index{CoHA!$\Eone$-chiral structure}
\index{CoHA!factorization structure}

The CoHA product (Definition~\ref{def:coha}) is defined via Hecke
correspondences on moduli of quiver representations.  Its factorization
structure---the assembly of $\mathcal{H}_Q = \bigoplus_{\mathbf{d}}
H^{G_{\mathbf{d}}}_{\mathrm{BM},*}(\mathcal{M}_{\mathbf{d}}^{\mathrm{nil}})$
over all dimension vectors---is reminiscent of the factorization algebras
underlying vertex algebras.

\begin{conjecture}[CoHA--Yangian Koszul duality; \ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:coha-koszul}
\index{CoHA!Koszul duality}
For a quiver $Q$ whose underlying graph is the Dynkin diagram of a
simple Lie algebra $\fg_Q$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:coha-yangian-dual}
\mathcal{H}_Q^! \;\simeq\; Y(\fg_Q)
\end{equation}
as $\Eone$-algebras, where $\mathcal{H}_Q$ is the CoHA of $Q$
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:coha})} and $Y(\fg_Q)$ is the
Yangian \textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:yangian})}.
(Contributing to Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.)
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Scope and evidence]
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
\item For $Q = $ Jordan quiver (one vertex, one loop),
$\mathcal{H}_{\mathrm{Jordan}}$ is the shuffle algebra, which
is isomorphic to $U(\widehat{\mathfrak{gl}}_1)^+$
(Schiffmann--Vasserot \cite{SV13}).  Since $Y(\mathfrak{gl}_1)$
is the Yangian of $\mathfrak{gl}_1$ and
$\widehat{\mathfrak{gl}}_1 \cong \mathcal{H}_{\mathrm{Heis}}$,
the duality $\mathcal{H}_{\mathrm{Jordan}}^! \simeq Y(\mathfrak{gl}_1)$
reduces to the Heisenberg Koszul duality
$\mathcal{H}_k^! \simeq \mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:heisenberg-not-self-dual}; note:
$\mathcal{H}$ is \emph{not} self-dual).
\item The factorization structure of the CoHA over dimension vectors
$\mathbf{d}$ corresponds to the coproduct structure of the Yangian bar
complex: the Hecke correspondence $\mathcal{M}_{\mathbf{d}_1}
\xleftarrow{p} \mathcal{E} \xrightarrow{q}
\mathcal{M}_{\mathbf{d}_1 + \mathbf{d}_2}$ is the geometric analog
of the bar complex coproduct $\Delta\colon \barB^n \to
\bigoplus_{i+j=n} \barB^i \otimes \barB^j$.
\item At the level of generators, the bar cohomology classes of
$Y(\fg_Q)$ should correspond to CoHA generators via the identification
of the RTT bar differential (equation~\eqref{eq:yangian-bar-d2}) with
the Hecke product.  The quadratic RTT relations map to the quadratic
part of the shuffle product.
\end{enumerate}
A proof would require first establishing the $\Eone$-chiral structure
on $\mathcal{H}_Q$ (Conjecture~\ref{conj:coha-e1}) and then computing
its bar complex.

\emph{Homotopy template} (Convention~\ref{conv:hms-levels}): Type~II (equivalence).
The conjecture asserts a Koszul duality equivalence between the CoHA of a Dynkin quiver and the corresponding Yangian as $\Eone$-algebras.
\end{remark}


\section{Explicit Yangian bar complex computations}
\label{sec:yangian-bar-explicit}
\index{Yangian!bar complex!explicit}

\subsection{\texorpdfstring{RTT bar complex for $Y(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$}{RTT bar complex for Y(sl2)}}

\begin{computation}[Yangian \texorpdfstring{$Y(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$}{Y(sl_2)}: bar complex
through degree 3]
\label{comp:yangian-sl2-bar}
\index{Yangian!sl2@$\mathfrak{sl}_2$!bar complex}

The Yangian $Y(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ in Drinfeld's first realization
has generators $\{e_0, f_0, h_0, e_1, f_1, h_1\}$ with
relations encoding the $\mathfrak{sl}_2$ Lie algebra at level~0
and the Yangian deformation at level~1.

\emph{RTT presentation.}
In the RTT formalism (Definition~\ref{def:yangian-rtt}), the
algebra is generated by the matrix entries $t_{ij}^{(r)}$
($i,j \in \{1,2\}$, $r \geq 0$) of the generating matrix
$T(u) = \sum_{r \geq 0} T^{(r)} u^{-r}$ subject to
$R_{12}(u-v) T_1(u) T_2(v) = T_2(v) T_1(u) R_{12}(u-v)$,
where $R(u) = 1 - P/u$ is the rational $R$-matrix
($P$ is the permutation operator).

\emph{Degree 1.}
$\bar{B}^1(Y(\mathfrak{sl}_2))$ is spanned by the
generators $t_{ij}^{(r)}$ for all $r \geq 1$
(the augmentation ideal excludes $t_{ij}^{(0)} = \delta_{ij}$).
At filtration degree $\leq n$: $\dim \bar{B}^1_{\leq n}
= 4n$ (four matrix entries at each level $r = 1, \ldots, n$).

\emph{Degree 2.}
Elements $[t_{ij}^{(r)} | t_{kl}^{(s)}] \otimes \eta_{12}$
with $r, s \geq 1$.  The bar differential extracts the $R$-matrix
commutation relation:
\begin{align}
d\bigl([t_{ij}^{(r)} | t_{kl}^{(s)}] \otimes \eta_{12}\bigr)
&= \Res_{u = v}\left[
\frac{R_{12}(u-v)_{ij,kl} - \delta_{ij}\delta_{kl}}{u-v}
\right]_{r,s} \label{eq:yangian-bar-d2}
\end{align}
The $R$-matrix $R(u) = 1 - P/u$ gives:
\[
\frac{R(u)_{ij,kl} - \delta_{ij}\delta_{kl}}{u}
= -\frac{\delta_{il}\delta_{kj}}{u^2}
\quad (\text{the permutation term})
\]
The residue at $u = v$ extracts the $1/(u-v)$ coefficient:
\begin{align}
d([t_{ij}^{(r)} | t_{kl}^{(s)}]) &=
-t_{il}^{(r+s-1)} \delta_{kj} + t_{kj}^{(r+s-1)} \delta_{il}
\label{eq:yangian-d2-explicit}
\end{align}
(the RTT relation at the level of generating functions).

\emph{Explicit at lowest levels.}
At $r = s = 1$:
\begin{align*}
d([t_{11}^{(1)} | t_{22}^{(1)}])
&= -t_{12}^{(1)} + t_{21}^{(1)} \\
d([t_{12}^{(1)} | t_{21}^{(1)}])
&= -t_{11}^{(1)} + t_{22}^{(1)} = -h_0^{(1)}
\end{align*}
where $h_0^{(1)} = t_{11}^{(1)} - t_{22}^{(1)}$ is the Cartan
generator at level~1.

\emph{Degree 3: Serre-type relations.}
At degree~3, the bar differential encodes the Yangian Serre
relations.  The key element:
\begin{align*}
d([e_1 | e_1 | f_1] \otimes \eta_{12} \wedge \eta_{13})
&= [e_1 | h_1] \otimes \eta_{13}
+ \text{(other terms)}
\end{align*}
The Serre relation
$[e_1, [e_1, f_0]] - [e_0, [e_1, f_1]] = \frac{1}{4}\{h_0, e_0\}$
appears as a cohomological relation in $H^3(\bar{B}(Y))$.

\emph{Dimension table.}
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{c|cccc}
Filtration degree & $\dim \bar{B}^1$ & $\dim \bar{B}^2$ &
$\dim \bar{B}^3$ & $\dim H^2$ \\
\hline
$\leq 1$ & 4 & 16 & 64 & 6 \\
$\leq 2$ & 8 & 64 & 512 & 22 \\
$\leq 3$ & 12 & 144 & 1728 & 42
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Note: the column ``$\dim H^2$'' reports the Koszul dual dimension
$(A^!)_2$ of the truncated RTT \emph{quadratic algebra}
$Y(\mathfrak{gl}_2)_{\leq L}$, which grows with the filtration
level~$L$.  This differs from the \emph{chiral} bar cohomology
$\dim H^2(\barBgeom(Y(\mathfrak{sl}_2)^{\mathrm{ch}})) = 10$
(Table~\ref{tab:bar-dimensions}), which uses
$4$ independent generators only (Remark~\ref{rem:yangian-gl2-kunneth}).
\end{computation}


\subsection{Yangian Koszul dual: explicit verification}

\begin{computation}[Yangian duality: \texorpdfstring{$R(u) \mapsto R(u)^{-1}$}{R(u) R(u)^-1}]
\label{comp:yangian-dual-explicit}
\index{Yangian!Koszul dual!explicit}

The $\Eone$-chiral Koszul duality of
Theorem~\ref{thm:yangian-koszul-dual}
sends $R(u)$ to~$R(u)^{-1}$.
For the rational~$R$-matrix:
\[
R(u) = 1 - \frac{P}{u}, \qquad
R(u)^{-1} = 1 + \frac{P}{u - 1}
= \frac{u}{u-1} - \frac{P}{u-1}
\]

\emph{Interpretation.}
The dual $R$-matrix $R(u)^{-1}$ defines the dual Yangian
$Y(\mathfrak{sl}_2)^!$ via the RTT relation
$R^{-1}_{12}(u-v) T_1(u) T_2(v)
= T_2(v) T_1(u) R^{-1}_{12}(u-v)$.

The pole of $R(u)^{-1}$ at $u = 1$ (rather than $u = 0$
for $R(u)$) shifts the ``interaction point'' in the bar complex.
The degree-2 bar differential~\eqref{eq:yangian-d2-explicit}
becomes:
\[
d^!([t_{ij}^{(r)} | t_{kl}^{(s)}])
= t_{il}^{(r+s)} \delta_{kj} - t_{kj}^{(r+s)} \delta_{il}
\]
(the shift $r+s-1 \mapsto r+s$ reflects the pole shift
$u = 0 \mapsto u = 1$).

\emph{Self-duality at the level of bar complexes.}
Theorem~\ref{thm:yangian-koszul-dual} proves $Y(\fg)^! \cong Y_{R^{-1}}(\fg)$
($R$-matrix inversion).  It is further expected---but not proved---that
$Y(\fg)$ is \emph{self-dual} after the spectral parameter shift
$u \mapsto u + 1$ (Conjecture~\ref{conj:yangian-spectral-selfdual}).
At the level of bar complexes, this amounts to the statement that the
bar complex with $R$-matrix $R(u)^{-1}$ is quasi-isomorphic to that
with $R$-matrix $R(u-1)$, which by the translation invariance
of the RTT relation is isomorphic to the original bar complex.

\begin{conjecture}[Spectral-shift self-duality; \ClaimStatusConjectured]\label{conj:yangian-spectral-selfdual}
For simply-laced $\fg$, the Koszul dual $Y(\fg)^! \cong Y_{R^{-1}}(\fg)$
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:yangian-koszul-dual}}\textup{)} is
isomorphic to $Y(\fg)$ itself after the spectral parameter shift
$u \mapsto u + 1$.
\end{conjecture}

\end{computation}

\begin{remark}[K\"unneth decomposition for \texorpdfstring{$\widehat{\mathfrak{gl}}_2$}{gl_2}]
\label{rem:yangian-gl2-kunneth}
\index{Yangian!Kunneth decomposition@K\"unneth decomposition}
In the chiral bar complex, the level-$1$ generators
$T_{ij}^{(1)}$ ($1 \leq i,j \leq 2$) span
$\mathfrak{gl}_2 = \mathfrak{sl}_2 \oplus \mathfrak{gl}_1$, and
the OPE among them reproduces the $\widehat{\mathfrak{gl}}_2$
current algebra (double pole from the level, simple pole from
the Lie bracket).  Higher-level generators $T_{ij}^{(r)}$
($r \geq 2$) appear as composites
(normal-ordered products of level-$1$ fields).
By the K\"unneth formula for bar complexes
of direct products:
\[
H^n(\barBgeom(\widehat{\mathfrak{gl}}_2))
= \sum_{i+j = n}
H^i(\barBgeom(\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2))
\otimes
H^j(\barBgeom(\widehat{\mathfrak{gl}}_1))
\]
with $H^i(\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2) = 3, 5, 15, 36, 91, \ldots$
(Table~\ref{tab:bar-dimensions}) and
$H^j(\widehat{\mathfrak{gl}}_1) = p(j{-}2)$ (partition function,
$p({-}1) = p(0) = 1$).  This gives
$H^n(\widehat{\mathfrak{gl}}_2) = 1, 4, 9, 24, 61, \ldots$
At degree~$1$, the Yangian bar cohomology matches
$\widehat{\mathfrak{gl}}_2$ exactly ($H^1 = 4$).
At degree~$2$, the Yangian exceeds the K\"unneth prediction:
$H^2(Y) = 10 > H^2(\widehat{\mathfrak{gl}}_2) = 9$.
At degree~$3$, the gap widens to $28 - 24 = 4$.
\end{remark}


\subsection{Coulomb branch bar complex}

\begin{computation}[Coulomb branch and Yangian bar]
\label{comp:coulomb-bar}
\index{Coulomb branch!bar complex}

For the Jordan quiver with dimension vector $\mathbf{d} = (n)$
and framing vector $\mathbf{w} = (1)$, the Coulomb branch
$\mathcal{M}_C(n, 1)$ is:
\[
\mathcal{M}_C(n, 1)
= \operatorname{Spec}\bigl(
\bC[z_1, \ldots, z_n]^{S_n}[\hbar]\bigr)
\cong \bC^n/S_n \times \bC_\hbar
\]
(the symmetric product of the affine line, quantized by $\hbar$).

The quantized Coulomb branch algebra
$A_\hbar(n, 1)$ is generated by
$e_k = \sum_{i=1}^n z_i^k$ ($k \geq 1$) with
the shifted Yangian relation:
\[
[e_k, e_l] = \hbar \cdot k \delta_{k+l, 0} \cdot n
+ \text{(lower terms)}
\]

\emph{Bar complex.}
The bar complex $\bar{B}(A_\hbar(n,1))$ has degree-2
elements $[e_k | e_l] \otimes \eta_{12}$ with differential:
\[
d([e_k | e_l]) = [e_k, e_l]
= \hbar k n \delta_{k+l} + \sum_{j=1}^{k-1}
\binom{k}{j} e_{k-j} e_{l+j} - (k \leftrightarrow l)
\]
At $n = 1$ (the Heisenberg case): $A_\hbar(1,1) \cong
\mathcal{H}_\hbar$ (the Heisenberg algebra at level $\hbar$),
and the bar complex reduces to the Heisenberg bar complex
of Computation~\ref{comp:heisenberg-deg3-full}.

At $n = 2$: the algebra $A_\hbar(2,1)$ contains both the
Heisenberg subalgebra (generated by $e_1 = z_1 + z_2$) and
a relative subalgebra (generated by $e_2 - e_1^2/2
= (z_1-z_2)^2/2$).  The bar complex detects the interaction
between these two sectors via the residue at the diagonal
$z_1 = z_2$ in the symmetric product.
\end{computation}


\section{Higher-rank Yangians and quantum groups}
\label{sec:higher-rank-yangians}
\index{Yangian!higher rank}

\subsection{\texorpdfstring{Yangian $Y(\mathfrak{sl}_3)$: bar complex}{Yangian Y(sl3): bar complex}}

\begin{computation}[\texorpdfstring{$Y(\mathfrak{sl}_3)$}{Y(sl_3)} bar complex through degree 2]
\label{comp:yangian-sl3-bar}
\index{Yangian!sl3@$\mathfrak{sl}_3$!bar complex}

The Yangian $Y(\mathfrak{sl}_3)$ is generated by the $3 \times 3$
matrix $T(u) = (t_{ij}(u))_{1 \leq i,j \leq 3}$ with
$t_{ij}(u) = \delta_{ij} + \sum_{r=1}^\infty t_{ij}^{(r)} u^{-r}$,
subject to the RTT relation with $R$-matrix
$R_{12}(u) = 1 - P_{12}/u$.

\emph{Degree 1.}
The generators $\{t_{ij}^{(r)} : 1 \leq i,j \leq 3, \; r \geq 1\}$
form the desuspended bar generators $s^{-1}t_{ij}^{(r)}$.
At filtration degree $\leq 1$: $\dim \bar{B}^1 = 9$
(the nine entries of the first-order matrix $T^{(1)}$).
At filtration degree $\leq n$: $\dim \bar{B}^1 = 9n$.

\emph{Degree 2.}
The bar differential encodes the RTT relation.
For generators at levels $r, s \geq 1$:
\begin{align*}
d([t_{ij}^{(r)} | t_{kl}^{(s)}])
&= t_{ij}^{(r)} t_{kl}^{(s)} - t_{kl}^{(s)} t_{ij}^{(r)} \\
&\quad - t_{kj}^{(r)} t_{il}^{(s-1)} + t_{il}^{(s)} t_{kj}^{(r-1)} \\
&= [t_{ij}^{(r)}, t_{kl}^{(s)}]
- t_{kj}^{(r)} t_{il}^{(s-1)} + t_{il}^{(s)} t_{kj}^{(r-1)}.
\end{align*}

\emph{Serre relations.}
For $\mathfrak{sl}_3$, the Serre relations are:
\[
[t_{12}^{(1)}, [t_{12}^{(1)}, t_{23}^{(1)}]] = 0, \qquad
[t_{23}^{(1)}, [t_{23}^{(1)}, t_{12}^{(1)}]] = 0.
\]
These appear as degree-3 bar cocycles: the element
$[t_{12}^{(1)} | t_{12}^{(1)} | t_{23}^{(1)}]
- 2[t_{12}^{(1)} | t_{23}^{(1)} | t_{12}^{(1)}]
+ [t_{23}^{(1)} | t_{12}^{(1)} | t_{12}^{(1)}]$
is exact in $\bar{B}^3$, reflecting the Serre relation.

\emph{Dimension table.}
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{c|ccc}
Filtration degree & $\dim \bar{B}^1$ & $\dim \bar{B}^2$ &
$\dim H^2$ \\
\hline
$\leq 1$ & 9 & 81 & 27 \\
$\leq 2$ & 18 & 324 & 99
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The degree-2 cohomology satisfies $\dim H^2 = 3 \dim H^2(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$
at each filtration level, reflecting the rank-2 structure.
\end{computation}

\begin{proposition}[Rank dependence of Yangian bar complex; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-rank-dependence}
\index{Yangian!bar complex!rank dependence}

For the Yangian $Y(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$ at filtration degree $\leq 1$:
\begin{enumerate}
\item $\dim \bar{B}^1 = N^2 - 1$ (the dimension of $\mathfrak{sl}_N$,
after removing the trace condition $\sum_i t_{ii}^{(r)} = 0$).
\item $\dim \bar{B}^2 = (N^2-1)^2$ (all pairs of generators).
\item $\dim H^2 = \dim \mathfrak{sl}_N \otimes \mathfrak{sl}_N / \mathrm{Im}(d_2)
= (N^2-1)^2 - \binom{N^2-1}{2} + \dim(\mathrm{Serre})$,
where $\mathrm{Serre}$ denotes the Serre relation space.
\item The growth rate is polynomial in $N$: $\dim \bar{B}^n = O(N^{2n})$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
(i) At filtration degree 1, the generators are
$\{t_{ij}^{(1)} : 1 \leq i,j \leq N\}$ modulo the trace
condition, giving $N^2 - 1$ generators (matching $\dim \mathfrak{sl}_N$).

(ii) The degree-2 bar space $\bar{B}^2$ is spanned by
$\{[t_{ij}^{(1)} | t_{kl}^{(1)}]\}$, giving $(N^2-1)^2$ elements.

(iii) The image of $d_2$ consists of the RTT relations at
level $(1,1)$: $[t_{ij}^{(1)}, t_{kl}^{(1)}] - \delta_{kj} t_{il}^{(1)}
+ \delta_{il} t_{kj}^{(1)}$.  These span a subspace of
dimension $(N^2-1)^2 - \dim H^2$, and $H^2 \cong \mathfrak{sl}_N[u]/(u^2)$
at this filtration level.

(iv) At filtration degree $\leq n$, $\dim \bar{B}^1 = (N^2-1)n$,
so $\dim \bar{B}^k = O(N^{2k} n^k)$.  For fixed $n$, this is
polynomial in $N$.
\end{proof}


\subsection{Quantum group connection}

\begin{remark}[Yangian vs quantum group bar complexes]
\label{rem:yangian-quantum-group}
\index{quantum group!bar complex}

The Yangian $Y(\fg)$ and the quantum group $U_q(\fg)$ are
related by the ``rational vs trigonometric'' dichotomy:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{l|cc}
& \textbf{Yangian $Y(\fg)$} & \textbf{$U_q(\hat{\fg})$} \\
\hline
$R$-matrix type & Rational: $R(u) = 1 - P/u$ &
Trigonometric: $R(u) = q^{u} P + q^{-u}(1-P)$ \\
Spectral parameter & Additive: $u - v$ & Multiplicative: $u/v$ \\
Bar propagator & $\eta_{ij} = d\log(z_i - z_j)$ &
$\omega_{ij} = d\log(z_i/z_j)$ \\
FM space & $\overline{\mathrm{FM}}_n(\mathbb{C})$ &
$\overline{\mathrm{FM}}_n(\mathbb{C}^\times)$ \\
Koszul dual & $Y_{R^{-1}}(\fg)$ & $U_{q^{-1}}(\hat{\fg})$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The bar complex of $U_q(\hat{\fg})$ uses the trigonometric
$R$-matrix as the degree-2 differential.  The FM compactification
$\overline{\mathrm{FM}}_n(\mathbb{C}^\times)$ replaces the
rational propagator $d\log(z_i - z_j)$ with the trigonometric
propagator $d\log(z_i/z_j)$, and the boundary strata of the
FM space encode the coproduct structure of the quantum group.

At the critical value $q = 1$, the quantum group degenerates to
the universal enveloping algebra $U(\fg)$ and the trigonometric
$R$-matrix becomes the identity, reducing the bar complex to
the ordinary Chevalley--Eilenberg complex.  This mirrors the
genus-0 critical level phenomenon for affine KM algebras
(Proposition~\ref{prop:km-bar-curvature} at $k = -h^\vee$):
in both cases, the universal MC class $\Theta = 0$ at the
critical parameter (Theorem~\ref{thm:explicit-theta}), the bar
complex becomes uncurved, and the bar-cobar adjunction gives
an honest equivalence.
\end{remark}


\subsection{Transfer matrix and Baxter Q-operator}

\begin{computation}[Transfer matrix in the bar complex]
\label{comp:transfer-matrix-bar}
\index{transfer matrix!bar complex}

The transfer matrix of the Yangian $Y(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ is:
\[
\mathcal{T}(u) = \operatorname{tr}_{\mathbb{C}^2} T(u)
= t_{11}(u) + t_{22}(u).
\]
This is a generating function for commuting elements:
$[\mathcal{T}(u), \mathcal{T}(v)] = 0$ for all $u, v$.

\emph{Bar complex interpretation.}
The commutativity $[\mathcal{T}(u), \mathcal{T}(v)] = 0$ means that
the degree-2 bar element
\[
[\mathcal{T}^{(r)} | \mathcal{T}^{(s)}] \in \bar{B}^2(Y(\mathfrak{sl}_2))
\]
is exact for all $r, s$:
$d[\mathcal{T}^{(r)} | \mathcal{T}^{(s)}] = [\mathcal{T}^{(r)},
\mathcal{T}^{(s)}] = 0$.
Thus the elements $[\mathcal{T}^{(r)} | \mathcal{T}^{(s)}]$
are \emph{bar cocycles}, defining classes in $H^2(\bar{B})$.
These classes are in fact trivial (exact) because
$\mathcal{T}^{(r)} = t_{11}^{(r)} + t_{22}^{(r)}$ is a sum
of generators, and:
\begin{align*}
d([t_{11}^{(r)} | t_{22}^{(s)}] + [t_{22}^{(s)} | t_{11}^{(r)}])
&= [t_{11}^{(r)}, t_{22}^{(s)}] + [t_{22}^{(s)}, t_{11}^{(r)}] = 0.
\end{align*}

The Baxter Q-operator $Q(u)$ satisfies
$\mathcal{T}(u) Q(u) = Q(u+1) + Q(u-1)$
(the TQ-relation).  In the bar complex, this relation
appears as a degree-2 cocycle condition with a shift
in the spectral parameter filtration.
\end{computation}


\section{Yangian representation theory and bar modules}
\label{sec:yangian-rep-bar}
\index{Yangian!representations}

\begin{definition}[Evaluation module]\label{def:evaluation-module}
\index{evaluation module|textbf}
For $a \in \mathbb{C}$ and $V$ a finite-dimensional
$\mathfrak{sl}_N$-representation, the \emph{evaluation module}
$V(a)$ of $Y(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$ is defined by:
\[
t_{ij}(u) \mapsto \delta_{ij} + \frac{\rho_{ij}}{u - a}
\]
where $\rho_{ij}$ is the $\mathfrak{sl}_N$-action on $V$.
The parameter $a$ is the \emph{evaluation point}.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Evaluation module bar complex; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:eval-module-bar}

The bar complex of the evaluation module $V(a)$ is the
Chevalley--Eilenberg complex of $\mathfrak{sl}_N$ acting on $V$,
shifted by the evaluation point:
\[
\bar{B}(Y(\mathfrak{sl}_N); V(a))
\simeq C^*(\mathfrak{sl}_N, V)
\]
as a chain complex, where the differential uses the
$\mathfrak{sl}_N$-action $\rho$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The evaluation homomorphism $\operatorname{ev}_a \colon Y(\mathfrak{sl}_N) \to U(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$
sends $t_{ij}^{(r)}$ to $\rho_{ij} \delta_{r,1}$ (all higher modes act trivially).
The bar complex of the module $V(a)$ is therefore determined by
the $\mathfrak{sl}_N$-action alone: the degree-$n$ bar differential
\[
d([v_1 | \cdots | v_n]) = \sum_{k} (-1)^k [\cdots | \rho(v_k) | \cdots]
+ \sum_{i < j} (-1)^{i+j} [\cdots | [v_i, v_j] | \cdots]
\]
is exactly the Chevalley--Eilenberg differential.  The evaluation
point $a$ appears only as a shift in the spectral parameter filtration
and does not affect the chain complex structure.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Tensor product of evaluation modules]
\label{rem:tensor-eval}
\index{evaluation module!tensor product}

For two evaluation modules $V(a)$ and $W(b)$ with $a \neq b$,
the tensor product $V(a) \otimes W(b)$ is again a Yangian module.
The bar complex of the tensor product is related to the bar complexes
of the factors by a K\"unneth-type formula:
\[
\bar{B}(Y; V(a) \otimes W(b)) \simeq
\bar{B}(Y; V(a)) \otimes_{\bar{B}(Y)} \bar{B}(Y; W(b))
\]
where the tensor product is taken over the bar construction.

When $a = b$ (coincident evaluation points), the tensor product
develops a pole: the $R$-matrix $R(a-b) = R(0) = 1 - P/0$ diverges.
This singularity corresponds to the non-semisimplicity of the tensor
product at coincident points, mirroring the diagonal singularity
in the FM compactification.  The resolution of this singularity
(the FM blow-up at the diagonal) produces the Yangian analog of
the bar complex propagator.
\end{remark}

\subsection{\texorpdfstring{Yangian category $\mathcal{O}$ from bar-cobar duality}{Yangian category O from bar-cobar duality}}
\label{sec:yangian-category-O}
\index{Yangian!category O}

We first fix the ambient category.

\begin{definition}[Yangian category \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal{O}$}{O}]
\label{def:yangian-category-O}
\index{Yangian!category O!definition}
For $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_N$, the \emph{Yangian category~$\mathcal{O}$}
$\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_N)}$ is the full subcategory of
$Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$-modules~$M$ satisfying:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $M$ is finitely generated over~$Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$;
\item $M$ has a weight decomposition
  $M = \bigoplus_{\mu \in \mathfrak{h}^*} M_\mu$ with
  finite-dimensional weight spaces;
\item the set of weights of~$M$ is contained in a finite union
  of cones $\{\mu \leq \lambda_i\}$ for the dominance order.
\end{enumerate}
The \emph{polynomial subcategory}
$\mathcal{O}_{\mathrm{poly}} \subset \mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar}$ is the
full subcategory of modules whose composition factors all have
polynomial highest $\ell$-weights in the sense of
Drinfeld~\cite{Drinfeld88}.  For $N = 2$, every simple in
$\mathcal{O}$ is finite-dimensional, so
$\mathcal{O}_{\mathrm{poly}} = \mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar}$.  For
$N \ge 3$, it is an open question whether
$\mathcal{O}_{\mathrm{poly}}$ exhausts $\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar}$
\textup{(}Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:catO-thick-generation-verification}}\textup{)}.
\end{definition}

The module Koszul duality of
Theorem~\ref{thm:e1-module-koszul-duality}, combined with
the evaluation module bar complex
(Proposition~\ref{prop:eval-module-bar}), yields a
BGG-type resolution theory for Yangian modules.

\begin{theorem}[Yangian BGG resolution; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:yangian-bgg}
\index{BGG resolution!Yangian}
For $\mathfrak{g} = \mathfrak{sl}_N$ and a finite-dimensional
irreducible $\mathfrak{g}$-module $L(\lambda)$, the evaluation
module $L(\lambda)(a)$ of $Y(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$ admits a
bar resolution:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:yangian-bgg}
\cdots \to \bar{B}_2(Y; L(\lambda)(a))
  \to \bar{B}_1(Y; L(\lambda)(a))
  \to L(\lambda)(a) \to 0
\end{equation}
where $\bar{B}_n(Y; L(\lambda)(a))
\simeq C^n(\mathfrak{sl}_N, L(\lambda))$
is the Chevalley--Eilenberg complex.  In particular:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The resolution length is $\dim \mathfrak{sl}_N
  = N^2 - 1$.
\item The terms are
  $\bar{B}_n \cong L(\lambda) \otimes
  \bigwedge^n \mathfrak{sl}_N^*$,
  with differentials given by the dual of the
  $\mathfrak{sl}_N$-action.
\item Under Koszul duality $\Phi\colon
  Y(\mathfrak{sl}_N)\text{-mod}
  \to Y_{-\hbar}(\mathfrak{sl}_N)\text{-comod}$,
  the resolution maps to the dual BGG resolution
  of $L(\lambda)(-a)$ for the Koszul dual Yangian
  \textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:yangian-module-koszul})}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Parts~(i) and~(ii) follow immediately from
Proposition~\ref{prop:eval-module-bar}: the bar complex
is the CE complex $C^*(\mathfrak{sl}_N, L(\lambda))$,
which has terms $L(\lambda) \otimes \bigwedge^n \mathfrak{sl}_N^*$
and length $\dim \mathfrak{sl}_N$.

For part~(iii): Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-module-koszul}
establishes $\Phi(V(a)_\hbar) = V(-a)_{-\hbar}$.
The bar-cobar functor $\Phi$ applied termwise to the
resolution~\eqref{eq:yangian-bgg} gives:
\[
\Phi(\bar{B}_n(Y_\hbar; L(\lambda)(a)))
\simeq \bar{B}_n(Y_{-\hbar}; L(\lambda)(-a))
\]
because $\Phi$ acts on the CE complex by inverting
$\hbar$ (which replaces $R$ by $R^{-1}$) and negating
the evaluation point.  The CE differential is
$\hbar$-independent (it depends only on the
$\mathfrak{sl}_N$-action), so the dual resolution
is isomorphic as a chain complex.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Ext exchange for Yangian modules;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:yangian-ext-exchange}
\index{Ext!Yangian modules}
For evaluation modules $L(\lambda)(a)$ and $L(\mu)(b)$
of $Y(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$:
\[
\operatorname{Ext}^n_{Y_\hbar}(L(\lambda)(a), L(\mu)(b))
\;\cong\;
\operatorname{Ext}^n_{Y_{-\hbar}}(L(\lambda)(-a), L(\mu)(-b))
\]
via the module Koszul duality functor $\Phi$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Theorem~\ref{thm:e1-module-koszul-duality}(ii),
$\operatorname{Ext}^n_{\cA}(L, M)
\cong \operatorname{Coext}^n_{\cA^!}(\Phi(M), \Phi(L))$.
For Yangian evaluation modules, $\Phi$ sends
$(L(\lambda)(a), \hbar)$ to $(L(\lambda)(-a), -\hbar)$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-module-koszul}).
Since $Y_{-\hbar}(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$ is again a Yangian
(with inverted deformation parameter), the Coext
groups are ordinary Ext groups for $Y_{-\hbar}$, giving
the stated isomorphism.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Conditional extension to full Yangian
category \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal{O}$}{O}]
\label{rem:yangian-cat-O-conditional}
The results above hold unconditionally for
evaluation modules (which reduce to finite-dimensional
$\mathfrak{sl}_N$-representations).  This is the endpoint of DK-1 in
Remark~\ref{rem:yangian-status}.  Extending to
the \emph{full} Yangian category~$\mathcal{O}$---which
includes infinite-dimensional highest-weight modules,
Verma modules $M(\lambda, a)$, and their subquotients---requires
the Koszulness conjecture
(Remark~\ref{rem:yangian-collapse-conj}).  If $Y(\mathfrak{g})$
is Koszul, then the bar spectral sequence collapses,
the bar complex provides minimal resolutions of
\emph{all} modules in $\mathcal{O}$, and the module
Koszul duality extends to an equivalence
$D^b(\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar}) \simeq
D^b(\mathcal{O}_{Y_{-\hbar}})$
sending $M(\lambda, a) \mapsto M(\lambda, -a)$.  The point is that the
remaining step is a generation/extension problem for the completed
ordered category, not a new computation on evaluation modules.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[DK-2 reduction to thick generation in
category~\texorpdfstring{$\mathcal{O}$}{O}; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk2-thick-generation}
Let
\[
\mathcal{D}_{\hbar}^{\mathrm{eval}}
\subset D^b(\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar}),
\qquad
\mathcal{D}_{-\hbar}^{\mathrm{eval}}
\subset D^b(\mathcal{O}_{Y_{-\hbar}})
\]
be the smallest thick triangulated subcategories containing all
evaluation modules.  Assume the module Koszul duality functor of
Theorem~\ref{thm:e1-module-koszul-duality} preserves the completed
Yangian categories $\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar}$ and
$\mathcal{O}_{Y_{-\hbar}}$ on the objects under consideration.  Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item the evaluation-module correspondence of
  Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-module-koszul} restricts to an exact
  equivalence
  \[
  \Phi_{\mathrm{eval,thick}}\colon
  \mathcal{D}_{\hbar}^{\mathrm{eval}}
  \xrightarrow{\sim}
  \mathcal{D}_{-\hbar}^{\mathrm{eval}};
  \]
\item if
  \[
  \mathcal{D}_{\hbar}^{\mathrm{eval}}
  = D^b(\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar}),
  \qquad
  \mathcal{D}_{-\hbar}^{\mathrm{eval}}
  = D^b(\mathcal{O}_{Y_{-\hbar}}),
  \]
  then the DK-2 extension from evaluation modules to the full
  completed Yangian category~$\mathcal{O}$ holds.
\end{enumerate}
In particular, once preservation of category~$\mathcal{O}$ is granted,
DK-2 is exactly a thick-generation problem for evaluation modules, not
a new local bar computation.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Because the module Koszul duality functor is exact, it preserves
shifts, cones, and direct summands.  Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-module-koszul}
identifies the images of all evaluation modules, so the functor carries
the smallest thick triangulated subcategory generated by them on the
$\hbar$-side onto the corresponding thick subcategory on the
$-\hbar$-side, and the inverse module functor does the reverse.  This
proves~\textup{(i)}.  Statement~\textup{(ii)} is immediate.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Thick generation by evaluation modules
in type~\texorpdfstring{$A$}{A}; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:dk2-thick-generation-typeA}
\index{Yangian!thick generation}
For $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_N$ with $N \ge 2$, every finite-dimensional
irreducible $Y(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$-module is a subquotient of a tensor
product of fundamental evaluation modules.  Consequently, the
thick triangulated subcategory
\[
\mathcal{D}_{\hbar}^{\mathrm{eval}}
\;\subset\;
D^b\bigl(\mathrm{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}(Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_N))\bigr)
\]
generated by evaluation modules equals
$D^b(\mathrm{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}(Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_N)))$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
We argue in three steps.

\emph{Step~1: Every simple is a subquotient of evaluation tensor
products.}
Let $L$ be a finite-dimensional irreducible
$Y(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$-module.  By the Drinfeld classification
\cite{Drinfeld88}, $L$ is determined by an $N$-tuple of monic
polynomials $(P_1(u), \ldots, P_{N-1}(u))$ (the Drinfeld
polynomials).  Write $P_i(u) = \prod_{j=1}^{d_i}(u - a_{ij})$.
The tensor product
\[
\bigotimes_{i=1}^{N-1}\; \bigotimes_{j=1}^{d_i}\;
V_{\omega_i}(a_{ij})
\]
of fundamental evaluation modules
$V_{\omega_i}(a) = \bigwedge^i \mathbb{C}^N(a)$ is a finite-dimensional
$Y(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$-module whose unique irreducible quotient (in a suitable
ordering of factors) has Drinfeld polynomials $(P_1, \ldots, P_{N-1})$
\cite{Drinfeld88}.  Hence $L$ is a quotient, and in particular a
subquotient, of a tensor product of fundamental evaluation modules.

\emph{Step~2: Every simple lies in the thick closure.}
Let $M = \bigotimes V_{\omega_i}(a_{ij})$ be the tensor product
from Step~1.  Since $M$ is finite-dimensional, it has a
finite composition series $0 = M_0 \subset M_1 \subset \cdots
\subset M_r = M$ with simple graded pieces
$M_k/M_{k-1} \cong L_k$.  Each short exact sequence
$0 \to M_{k-1} \to M_k \to L_k \to 0$ yields an exact triangle
$M_{k-1} \to M_k \to L_k \to M_{k-1}[1]$ in
$D^b(\mathrm{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}})$.  The tensor product~$M$ is itself
in the thick closure of evaluation modules (each factor
$V_{\omega_i}(a_{ij})$ is an evaluation module).  By descending
induction on the composition series, every composition factor~$L_k$
lies in the thick closure.

\emph{Step~3: All objects lie in the thick closure.}
An arbitrary object $X \in D^b(\mathrm{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}})$ is a
bounded complex of finite-dimensional modules, each of finite length
with simple factors.  By Step~2, every simple is in the thick closure
$\mathcal{D}_{\hbar}^{\mathrm{eval}}$.  A thick subcategory of a
triangulated category is closed under extensions (via the octahedral
axiom) and bounded complexes (via iterated cones), so all of
$D^b(\mathrm{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}})$ is contained in
$\mathcal{D}_{\hbar}^{\mathrm{eval}}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Thick generation and DK-2]
\label{rem:dk2-thick-generation-consequence}
Proposition~\ref{prop:dk2-thick-generation-typeA} verifies
hypothesis~(ii) of Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk2-thick-generation}
for the finite-dimensional regime.  The remaining DK-2 gap for
type~$A$ is therefore:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Preservation}: the module Koszul duality functor~$\Phi$
  of Theorem~\ref{thm:e1-module-koszul-duality} must preserve
  category~$\mathcal{O}$, not just finite-dimensional modules; and
\item \emph{Infinite-dimensional extension}: thick generation of
  $D^b(\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar})$ by evaluation modules, extending
  the finite-dimensional result to Verma modules and their
  subquotients.
\end{enumerate}
For~(a), the key input would be that~$\Phi$ respects the weight
filtration (which it does on evaluation modules by
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-module-koszul}).  For~(b), the standard
BGG resolution of a Verma module $M(\lambda, a)$ by direct sums of
Verma modules, combined with the fact that Verma modules at generic
highest weight are evaluation-module images under parabolic induction,
reduces this to the well-studied structure of Yangian
category~$\mathcal{O}$.

The type~$A$ thick generation result also
verifies the finite-dimensional part of the full-generation
hypothesis needed for
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk3-generated-core} \textup{(}DK-3\textup{)}.
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[Thick generation from finite composition series;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{lem:composition-thick-generation}
\index{thick generation!from composition series}
Let $\cA$ be an Artinian abelian category and
$\cC \subset D^b(\cA)$ a thick triangulated subcategory containing
every simple object of~$\cA$ (viewed in degree~$0$).  Then
$\cC = D^b(\cA)$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step~1: Objects of $\cA$ lie in~$\cC$.}
Every $M \in \cA$ has a finite composition series
$0 = M_0 \subset M_1 \subset \cdots \subset M_r = M$
with each $M_i/M_{i-1}$ simple, hence in~$\cC$ by hypothesis.
We argue by induction on~$r$.  For $r = 0$, $M = 0 \in \cC$.
For $r \ge 1$, the short exact sequence
$0 \to M_{r-1} \to M \to M_r/M_{r-1} \to 0$
yields a distinguished triangle
$M_{r-1} \to M \to M_r/M_{r-1} \xrightarrow{+1}$
in $D^b(\cA)$.
The outer terms lie in~$\cC$ (by induction and hypothesis),
so $M \in \cC$ since thick subcategories are closed under cones.

\emph{Step~2: Bounded complexes.}
For a bounded complex $C = [C^a \to \cdots \to C^b]$ with
$C^i \in \cA$, the stupid truncation triangle
$\sigma_{\ge a+1}C \to C \to C^a[-a] \xrightarrow{+1}$
and induction on the amplitude $b - a$ give $C \in \cC$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Thick generation of category~\texorpdfstring{$\mathcal{O}$}{O} by
evaluation modules, type~\texorpdfstring{$A$}{A}; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:catO-thick-generation}
\index{thick generation!Category O@Category $\mathcal{O}$|textbf}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!derived!Category O@Category $\mathcal{O}$}
For $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_N$ with $N \ge 2$, let
$\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar}$ be a full subcategory of
$\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_N)}$ satisfying:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item $\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar}$ is Artinian
  \textup{(}every object has finite composition length\textup{)};
\item every simple object of $\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar}$ is
  finite-dimensional.
\end{enumerate}
Then the thick triangulated subcategory
$\mathcal{D}_\hbar^{\mathrm{eval}} \subset
D^b(\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar})$
generated by evaluation modules equals
$D^b(\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar})$.
Consequently, DK-2
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:yangian-dk2-thick-generation}}\textup{)}
holds for~$\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar}$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:dk2-thick-generation-typeA}, every
finite-dimensional simple $Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$-module lies in
$\mathcal{D}_\hbar^{\mathrm{eval}}$.
Hypothesis~(b) then gives that every simple of
$\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar}$ lies in
$\mathcal{D}_\hbar^{\mathrm{eval}}$.
Hypothesis~(a) and Lemma~\ref{lem:composition-thick-generation}
yield $D^b(\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar}) =
\mathcal{D}_\hbar^{\mathrm{eval}}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Verification of hypotheses and scope]
\label{rem:catO-thick-generation-verification}
\index{Category O@Category $\mathcal{O}$!finite-dimensionality of simples}
Hypotheses (a) and~(b) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:catO-thick-generation} hold in the following
settings:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{$N = 2$.}
  Category~$\mathcal{O}$ for $Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$
  is controlled by Kirillov--Reshetikhin modules:
  every module has finite composition length
  with finite-dimensional factors
  \cite{ChariPressley94}.
  Thick generation is therefore
  \emph{unconditional} for~$\mathfrak{sl}_2$.
\item \emph{Polynomial category~$\mathcal{O}$, any~$N$.}
  The Hernandez--Leclerc subcategory
  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathrm{poly}} \subset
  \mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_N)}$---modules
  with polynomial highest $\ell$-weights
  \cite{HernandezLeclerc10}---has all simple objects
  finite-dimensional by the Drinfeld classification
  \cite{Drinfeld88}.  Hence thick generation holds
  unconditionally for $\mathcal{O}_{\mathrm{poly}}$ at
  all~$N$.
\item \emph{Full category~$\mathcal{O}$ at $N \ge 3$.}
  The remaining question is whether the polynomial subcategory
  exhausts the full category~$\mathcal{O}$ relevant to the
  DK problem, or equivalently, whether every simple module in
  the DK-relevant category~$\mathcal{O}$ is finite-dimensional.
  For the factorization DK problem, the polynomial subcategory
  is the natural candidate.
\end{enumerate}
