\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))^{\mathrm{op}},
\end{equation}
where $\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{g})$ is the Yangian
$\Eone$-chiral algebra and $U_q(\mathfrak{g})$ is the quantum
group, viewed as an $\Eone$-factorization algebra via the
construction of Latyntsev~\cite{Latyntsev23}.
This is the factorization-level Kazhdan bridge beyond the evaluation
subcategories; it separates the ordered Yangian factorization problem
from the later dg-shifted comparison of
Conjecture~\ref{conj:full-dk-bridge}.
(Contributing to Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.)
\end{conjecture}

\begin{proposition}[DK-3 reduction to evaluation-generated
factorization cores; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk3-generated-core}
Let
\[
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{g}))
\subset \operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}(\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{g})),
\qquad
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))
\subset \operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))
\]
be the smallest full stable idempotent-complete braided monoidal
subcategories containing all ordered tensor products of evaluation
objects.  Assume there exist exact braided monoidal functors
\[
KZ_{\mathrm{fact}}^{\mathrm{gen}}\colon
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{g}))
\to
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))^{\mathrm{op}},
\]
\[
LZ_{\mathrm{fact}}^{\mathrm{gen}}\colon
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))^{\mathrm{op}}
\to
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{g})),
\]
whose restrictions to the evaluation generators recover the
evaluation-locus comparison of
Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval} after transport to the
quantum-group evaluation side, and such that both composites are
isomorphic to the identity on those generators.  Then the two functors
are quasi-inverse braided monoidal equivalences on the generated cores.
If, in addition,
\[
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{g}))
=
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}(\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{g})),
\qquad
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))
=
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}(U_q(\mathfrak{g})),
\]
then Conjecture~\ref{conj:full-derived-dk} holds.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The generated cores are obtained from the evaluation generators by
finite iterates of shifts, cones, direct summands, and ordered tensor
products.  Exact braided monoidal functors preserve each of these
operations.  Therefore any natural transformation between exact
braided monoidal functors that is an isomorphism on the evaluation
generators remains an isomorphism on the full generated cores.  Applying
this to the two composites shows that they are naturally isomorphic to
the identity on the generated cores, hence the two functors are
quasi-inverse equivalences there.  The final sentence is immediate.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Exact extra inputs for DK-2/DK-3]
\label{rem:yangian-dk23-inputs}
Propositions~\ref{prop:yangian-dk2-thick-generation}
and~\ref{prop:yangian-dk3-generated-core} make the remaining Yangian
DK inputs exact.  After the evaluation-locus theorem, the live extra
packets are:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item preservation or replacement resolution theory on the completed
  Yangian categories~$\mathcal{O}$;
\item thick generation of those derived categories by evaluation
  modules --- proved in type~A
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:dk2-thick-generation-typeA});
\item construction of the ordered factorization Kazhdan transport on
  the evaluation-generated factorization core --- a natural candidate
  is identified (Proposition~\ref{prop:bar-cobar-kazhdan-candidate});
  what remains is strict factorization-monoidal enhancement
  (Remark~\ref{rem:dk3-remaining-after-barcobar}); and
\item a reconstruction argument, Barr--Beck style or equivalent,
  producing the quasi-inverse pair on that core.
\end{enumerate}
For finite-dimensional representations in type~$A$,
items~(ii)--(iv) are resolved by
Theorem~\ref{thm:dk-fd-typeA}: thick generation
(Proposition~\ref{prop:dk2-thick-generation-typeA}) eliminates~(ii),
and the monoidal thick extension
(Lemma~\ref{lem:monoidal-thick-extension}) resolves~(iii)--(iv)
by extending the evaluation-level data to the thick closure.
The live extra packets are therefore:
(i)~preservation for category~$\mathcal{O}$ and
thick generation beyond $\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}$.
None of these is a new residue computation on evaluation modules.  The
residue/RTT identities begin only at the downstream DK-4/MC4 boundary.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[DK ladder: what is proved and what remains]
\label{rem:dk-proved-vs-remains}
\textbf{DK-0/1}: chain-level braided bar-cobar (Theorems~\ref{thm:e1-chiral-koszul-duality}--\ref{thm:derived-dk-yangian}) and evaluation-locus factorization DK (Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}) --- proved.  \textbf{DK-2/3}: evaluation-generated core, all simple types --- proved by thick generation in type~$A$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:dk-fd-typeA}) and sectorwise convergence for all types (Corollary~\ref{cor:dk23-all-types}); category-$\mathcal{O}$ extension conjectural (Conjecture~\ref{conj:full-derived-dk}, reduces to thick generation by Corollary~\ref{cor:dk-partial-conj}).  \textbf{DK-4/5}: conjectural (Conjecture~\ref{conj:full-dk-bridge}; see Remark~\ref{rem:yangian-dk23-inputs} for exact inputs).  Contributing to Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.
\end{remark}

\subsection{$\infty$-categorical factorization Koszul duality}
\label{sec:infty-cat-factorization-kd}
\index{Koszul duality!factorization!infinity-categorical@$\infty$-categorical|textbf}

The DK ladder as formulated in
Remark~\ref{rem:dk-proved-vs-remains} decomposes the factorization
Koszul duality problem into five stages, with DK-0/1/2/3 proved on the evaluation-generated
core at all simple types and DK-4/5 conjectural.  From first principles, the
entire ladder is a single $\infty$-categorical statement: Koszul
duality for $\Eone$-algebras in the symmetric monoidal stable
$\infty$-category of factorization coalgebras on~$\operatorname{Ran}(X)$.
We make this precise and show that DK-2/3 extends to the
evaluation-generated core at all types via
sectorwise convergence, bypassing thick generation, and that DK-4/5
reduces to a formal deformation theory comparison within the same
framework.

\subsubsection*{Sectorwise convergence and DK-2/3 for the evaluation-generated core at all types}

\begin{theorem}[Sectorwise spectral convergence;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:sectorwise-spectral-convergence}
\index{spectral sequence!sectorwise convergence}
\index{bar complex!sectorwise convergence}
For any simple~$\fg$, the loop spectral sequence of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-bar-loop-weight} stabilizes at each
tridegree: for each $\gamma \in Q(\fg)$ and each $(p,q)$, there
exists~$r_0 = r_0(p,q,\gamma) < \infty$ such that
\[
E_\infty^{p,q}(\barB_\gamma^{\mathrm{fact}})
\;=\; E_{r_0}^{p,q}(\barB_\gamma^{\mathrm{fact}}).
\]
Moreover:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item $\dim {E_\infty}^{p,q}_\gamma \le \dim {E_1}^{p,q}_\gamma$ at each
  tridegree, so the $E_\infty$ page inherits the sub-exponential
  growth bound of
  Proposition~\ref{prop:lqt-e1-subexponential-growth};
\item the $E_\infty$ page carries a well-defined factorization
  coalgebra structure, compatible with the $Q(\fg)$-grading
  and the factorization isomorphisms on
  $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Each ${E_0}^{p,q}_\gamma$ is finite-dimensional
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-bar-loop-weight}(c)).  Since
${E_{r+1}}^{p,q}$ is a subquotient of ${E_r}^{p,q}$, the sequence
$\dim {E_r}^{p,q}_\gamma$ is non-increasing and non-negative, hence
eventually constant.  This gives the first claim and~(a).

For~(b): by Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-bar-loop-weight}(a,b),
the factorization coalgebra structure on $\barB^{\mathrm{fact}}$
preserves the $Q(\fg)$-grading and is compatible with the loop
filtration~$F^\bullet$; it therefore descends to each page~$E_r$
and to~$E_\infty$.
\end{proof}

The sectorwise convergence is the key finiteness input for extending
the bar-cobar equivalence from the diagonal to the full
$\operatorname{Ran}$ space.  The argument generalizes the
lattice bypass of DK-$1\frac{1}{2}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:lattice:factorization-koszul}): in the lattice
case, $E_1 = 0$ (Heisenberg acyclicity) gave immediate degeneration;
here the $E_\infty$ page is nontrivial but finite-dimensional, which
suffices for the factorization descent.

\begin{theorem}[\texorpdfstring{$\infty$}{infinity}-categorical factorization Koszul duality
via sectorwise convergence; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}
\index{Koszul duality!factorization!sectorwise|textbf}
\index{sectorwise finiteness!factorization Koszul duality}
Let~$\cA$ be an $\Eone$-chiral algebra on a smooth curve~$X$
satisfying:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(H\arabic*)}]
\item\label{h1:koszulness} \emph{$\Eone$-Koszulness}: the cobar-bar
  counit
  $\Omega(\barB(\cA)) \to \cA$ is a quasi-isomorphism
  \textup{(}Theorem~B on the Koszul locus\textup{)};
\item\label{h2:sectorwise} \emph{Sectorwise finiteness}: the
  factorization bar complex $\barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA)$ admits a
  $\Gamma$-grading \textup{(}for a finitely generated abelian
  group~$\Gamma$\textup{)} and a descending
  filtration~$F^\bullet$ compatible with the grading, such that
  $\operatorname{gr}^p \barB_\gamma$ is finite-dimensional
  over each $\operatorname{Ran}$-stratum;
\item\label{h3:convergence} \emph{Spectral convergence}: the
  associated spectral sequence stabilizes at each tridegree
  \textup{(}automatic by
  Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:sectorwise-spectral-convergence}}
  when~\ref{h2:sectorwise} holds\textup{)}.
\end{enumerate}
Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The factorization bar-cobar counit
  \[
  \varepsilon^{\mathrm{fact}}\colon
  \Omega^{\mathrm{fact}}(\barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA)) \to \cA
  \]
  is a quasi-isomorphism of factorization algebras on
  $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$.
\item The factorization Verdier intertwining
  $\mathbb{D}_{\mathrm{Ran}}\,
  \barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA)
  \simeq \barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA^!)$
  holds at the factorization level.
\item The module bar functor
  \[
  \barB_{\mathrm{mod}}^{\mathrm{fact}}\colon
  \operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\cA)
  \to
  \operatorname{CoFact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}
    (\cA^{!,c})^{\mathrm{op}}
  \]
  is an equivalence of stable $\infty$-categories on the
  evaluation-generated cores, with braiding reversal
  $R \mapsto R^{-1}$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Part~(i): factorization bar-cobar.}
On the diagonal stratum $\operatorname{Ran}_1(X) \cong X$, the
factorization counit $\varepsilon^{\mathrm{fact}}$ restricts to
the ordinary cobar-bar counit
$\varepsilon\colon \Omega(\barB(\cA)) \to \cA$,
which is a quasi-isomorphism by hypothesis~\ref{h1:koszulness}
(Theorem~B).

For $n \ge 2$ and disjoint opens
$U_1, \ldots, U_k \subset X$, the factorization isomorphisms
decompose both source and target:
\begin{align*}
\Omega^{\mathrm{fact}}(\barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA))
  (U_1 \sqcup \cdots \sqcup U_k)
&\cong \bigotimes_{j=1}^k
  \Omega^{\mathrm{fact}}(\barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA))(U_j), \\
\cA(U_1 \sqcup \cdots \sqcup U_k)
&\cong \bigotimes_{j=1}^k \cA(U_j).
\end{align*}
The counit decomposes as $\varepsilon^{\mathrm{fact}}
= \varepsilon|_{U_1} \otimes \cdots \otimes \varepsilon|_{U_k}$,
and each factor $\varepsilon|_{U_j}$ is a quasi-isomorphism
by hypothesis~\ref{h1:koszulness} on the single-point stratum;
the K\"unneth formula for derived tensor products of chain
complexes over a field preserves quasi-isomorphisms, so the
tensor product is a quasi-isomorphism.

On arbitrary opens (including overlapping configurations), the
factorization algebra is determined by descent: a factorization
algebra on~$\operatorname{Ran}(X)$ is a cosheaf for the
factorization topology, whose basis consists of products of disjoint
opens.  Sectorwise finiteness~\ref{h2:sectorwise} guarantees that
$\barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA)$ is a genuine factorization coalgebra
on~$\operatorname{Ran}(X)$ (not merely a formal pro-object), so
the cosheaf condition applies.  A map of factorization cosheaves
that is a quasi-isomorphism on every basis open is a global
quasi-isomorphism, giving~(i).

\emph{Part~(ii): Verdier intertwining.}
The Verdier intertwining on~$\operatorname{Ran}_1$ is
Theorem~A\textsubscript{2}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-verdier}).
For disjoint opens
$U_1 \sqcup \cdots \sqcup U_k$, Verdier duality distributes as
$\mathbb{D}_{\mathrm{Ran}}
\simeq \mathbb{D}_{U_1} \boxtimes \cdots \boxtimes \mathbb{D}_{U_k}$,
so the factorization bar intertwining decomposes into a tensor
product of the $\operatorname{Ran}_1$ intertwining on each factor.
The same cosheaf descent as part~(i) extends from disjoint to
arbitrary opens.

\emph{Part~(iii): module equivalence.}
On evaluation objects, the module bar functor is an equivalence by
DK-1 (Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}).  The
evaluation-generated core
$\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\cA)$ is the
smallest full stable idempotent-complete braided monoidal subcategory
containing all evaluation objects.  Since the module bar functor
is exact and braided monoidal with reversal
(Theorem~\ref{thm:monoidal-module-koszul}), it preserves shifts,
cones, direct summands, and ordered tensor products.  Therefore, by
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk3-generated-core}, any natural
isomorphism between the identity and
$\Omega_{\mathrm{mod}} \circ \barB_{\mathrm{mod}}$ that holds on
evaluation generators extends to the full generated core.

The braiding reversal $R \mapsto R^{-1}$ is
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-module-koszul}(iii), extended to the
generated core by functoriality.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope of ``unconditional'']
\label{rem:dk23-unconditional-scope}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!unconditional!scope}
The following corollary is ``unconditional'' in the sense that it
does not require thick generation: the sectorwise convergence
argument works for all simple types without identifying the
generated core with $D^b(\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}})$.
It does, however, depend on the classical Koszulness of the RTT
Yangian (Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-koszul}), whose proof
uses Molev's PBW theorem \cite{molev-yangians} as external input.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[DK-2/3 for all simple types via sectorwise
convergence; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:dk23-all-types}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!derived!all types}
\index{sectorwise finiteness!DK for all types}
For $\fg$ any simple Lie algebra, the factorization bar-cobar
functor induces an equivalence on the evaluation-generated cores:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:dk23-all-types}
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}
  (Y_\hbar(\fg))
\;\xrightarrow{\;\sim\;}\;
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}
  (Y_{-\hbar}(\fg))^{\mathrm{op}},
\end{equation}
extending the evaluation-locus DK equivalence
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}}\textup{)}
to the full generated core at all types, without any
thick-generation argument.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Apply Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd} to
$\cA = \mathcal{Y}(\fg)$.
Hypothesis~\ref{h1:koszulness} is
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-bar-cobar}: the RTT Yangian is
quadratic, pro-nilpotent, and Koszul
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-koszul}), so
Theorem~\ref{thm:e1-chiral-koszul-duality} gives the
$\Eone$-chiral bar-cobar quasi-isomorphism for every
simple~$\fg$.
Hypothesis~\ref{h2:sectorwise} is
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-bar-loop-weight}: the $Q(\fg)$-grading
and loop filtration give the required sectorwise-finite bifiltration
for every simple~$\fg$.
Hypothesis~\ref{h3:convergence} follows from
Theorem~\ref{thm:sectorwise-spectral-convergence}.
Conclusion~(iii) gives~\eqref{eq:dk23-all-types}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[H/M/S semantic levels for DK-2/3]
\label{rem:dk23-hms}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!H/M/S levels}
\emph{Step~A} (H-level):
Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd} asserts an
equivalence of stable $\infty$-categories
$\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\cA)
\simeq
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\cA^!)^{\mathrm{op}}$
on the evaluation-generated cores, with braiding reversal
$R \mapsto R^{-1}$.  This is the theorem.

\emph{Step~B} (M-level):
The proof is a dg chain-level argument: sectorwise convergence
of the bar spectral sequence on each
$\operatorname{Ran}$-stratum, extended to the full factorization
cosheaf by descent.  Concretely, the module bar functor is exact
and braided monoidal
(Theorem~\ref{thm:monoidal-module-koszul}), and the
quasi-isomorphism on evaluation generators extends to the
generated core by functoriality
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk3-generated-core}).

\emph{Reduction B$\to$A} (M-level $\to$ H-level):
The dg descent implies the $\infty$-categorical equivalence: a
map of factorization cosheaves that is a quasi-isomorphism on
every basis open is a global quasi-isomorphism in the
$\infty$-categorical sense
(Lurie~\cite[Proposition~5.5.2.2]{HA}).  Thus the M-level
sectorwise quasi-isomorphisms determine the H-level equivalence
of stable $\infty$-categories.

\emph{Step~C} (S-level):
The shadow is the equality of graded dimensions
$\dim \operatorname{Ext}^i_{\cA}(V_\lambda, V_\mu)
= \dim \operatorname{Ext}^i_{\cA^!}(V_\lambda^!, V_\mu^!)$
across evaluation modules, together with the Kazhdan--Lusztig
multiplicity formula transported to the Koszul dual side.

\emph{Reduction B$\to$C} (M-level $\to$ S-level):
Taking cohomology of the M-level module bar complex
$\bar{B}_{\mathrm{mod}}(M)$ extracts the S-level Ext groups.
The sectorwise spectral sequence
(Theorem~\ref{thm:sectorwise-spectral-convergence}) converges
at each tridegree, so the M-level quasi-isomorphism on
evaluation generators yields isomorphisms of Ext groups.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Two proofs in type~\texorpdfstring{$A$}{A}; scope comparison]
\label{rem:two-dk-proofs}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!two proofs}
For $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_N$, there are now two independent proofs
of DK-2/3 on the evaluation-generated core:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Thick generation}
  \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:dk-fd-typeA}\textup{)}: uses the
  Drinfeld polynomial classification to show that evaluation modules
  generate all finite-dimensional simples, then the composition-length
  argument of Lemma~\ref{lem:composition-thick-generation}.  This proof
  is representation-theoretic and specific to type~$A$.
\item \emph{Sectorwise convergence}
  \textup{(}Corollary~\ref{cor:dk23-all-types}\textup{)}: uses
  the root lattice grading and loop filtration to bypass thick
  generation entirely.  The proof is
  operadic/factorization-theoretic and works for all types.
\end{enumerate}
Proof~(b) is strictly more general (all types $A$--$G$),
but proof~(a) is more explicit: it identifies the generated core as
$D^b(\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}})$ via the Drinfeld
classification.  Proof~(b) identifies the generated core as the
thick closure of evaluation objects in the factorization category,
without naming the individual simples.
The two proofs agree on type~$A$: thick generation by evaluation
modules (Proposition~\ref{prop:dk2-thick-generation-typeA})
identifies the two generated cores.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Interaction with the four-conjecture package]
\label{rem:h-level-vs-four-conjectures}
\index{MC3!four-conjecture package!interaction with H-level}
Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd} and
Corollary~\ref{cor:dk23-all-types} resolve DK-2/3 for the
evaluation-generated core at all types.  The four conjectures of
Remark~\ref{rem:corrected-mc3-frontier}(b) ---
Baxter exact triangles
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:baxter-exact-triangles}),
shifted-prefundamental generation
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:shifted-prefundamental-generation}),
pro-Weyl recovery (Conjecture~\ref{conj:pro-weyl-recovery}), and
DK on compacts
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk-compacts-completion}) ---
concern the extension \emph{beyond} this core to
infinite-dimensional modules via a completed or coderived
enhancement.

The two programmes are complementary:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item The sectorwise convergence theorem gives the strongest
  factorization equivalence on the natural domain
  (evaluation-generated core) at all types.
\item The four-conjecture package enlarges the domain to include
  prefundamental and asymptotic modules, requiring new input
  (Baxter TQ-lifts, pro-Weyl limits) beyond Koszul duality.
\item The formal moduli framework below provides the categorical
  home for both programmes: the evaluation-generated core is the
  compact part of the formal moduli problem, and the four-conjecture
  package extends to the completed/ind-completed part.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{DK-4/5 as formal moduli Koszul duality}

The passage from DK-3 to DK-4/5 --- from the evaluation-generated
core to the full triple bridge --- gains conceptual clarity when
viewed through the lens of formal moduli problems for
$\Eone$-algebras.  The abstract framework exists
unconditionally (Lurie~\cite{LurieDAGX}); the content of DK-4 is
the identification of the tangent Lie algebra with the dg-shifted
Yangian, and DK-5 is the passage from Lie algebra modules to group
representations.

\begin{definition}[Factorization formal moduli problem]
\label{def:factorization-formal-moduli}
\index{formal moduli problem!factorization|textbf}
For an $\Eone$-chiral algebra~$\cA$ on~$X$, the
\emph{factorization formal moduli problem} is the functor
\[
\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}\colon
\mathrm{CAlg}^{\mathrm{aug}}_{k}
\to \mathcal{S},
\qquad
R \;\mapsto\;
\operatorname{Map}_{\mathrm{FAlg}_{\Eone}(X)}
  \bigl(\cA \otimes R,\, \cA \otimes R\bigr)^{\simeq}
\]
from augmented commutative $k$-algebras to spaces, where the mapping
space is taken in the $\infty$-category of
$\Eone$-factorization algebras on~$\operatorname{Ran}(X)$.

By Lurie's formal moduli theorem~\cite{LurieDAGX},
$\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$ is controlled by a dg Lie algebra
$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA} := T_{*}\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$,
the \emph{tangent Lie algebra} of the moduli problem.
The bar complex provides the chain-level model:
$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA} \simeq
\operatorname{Der}(\barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA))$,
the derivations of the factorization bar coalgebra.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Canonical Yangian H-level dg target from factorization
formal moduli; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-canonical-hlevel-target}
For every $\Eone$-chiral algebra $\cA$ on~$X$, the factorization
formal moduli problem $\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$ of
Definition~\ref{def:factorization-formal-moduli} has a tangent dg Lie
algebra
\[
\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}:=T_*\mathfrak{F}_{\cA},
\]
and hence a canonically attached completed module category
\[
\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}).
\]
For the Yangian $\Eone$-chiral algebra
\[
\cA=\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{sl}_N),
\]
this gives an unconditional H-level dg target for DK-4/5.

Equivalently, the live Yangian MC4 problem is not the existence of an
H-level dg target.  It is the identification of this canonical formal
moduli target with an RTT-adapted dg model whose finite quotients
recover the theorematic RTT stages and whose degree-$2$ twisting
morphism matches the ordered bar seed on the fundamental line.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Existence of the tangent dg Lie algebra $\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$ is exactly
the content of Lurie's formal moduli theorem, as recalled in
Definition~\ref{def:factorization-formal-moduli}.  The completed module
category $\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})$ is
therefore canonically attached to $\cA$.  Specializing to the Yangian
$\Eone$-chiral algebra gives the claimed H-level target.

The remaining sentence is a reformulation of the Yangian MC4 frontier:
the unresolved step is to identify the canonical target
$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$ with an RTT-adapted dg model, not to construct the
target itself.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Canonical associative dg model of the Yangian
formal-moduli target; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-canonical-envelope}
Let
\[
\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}:=T_*\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}
\]
be the tangent dg Lie algebra of the factorization formal moduli
problem.  Let
\[
U^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})
\]
denote the completion of its universal enveloping dg algebra with
respect to the adic filtration defining complete
$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$-modules.  Then
$U^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})$ is a canonically attached
separated complete dg algebra, and there is a canonical equivalence
\[
\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})
\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}\bigl(
  U^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})
\bigr).
\]
For the Yangian $\Eone$-chiral algebra, this gives an unconditional
canonical associative dg model of the H-level target.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The universal enveloping construction extends functorially to dg Lie
algebras.  Completing with respect to the same adic filtration that
defines the completed module category of the formal moduli problem
produces a separated complete dg algebra
$U^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})$.

By the universal property of the enveloping algebra, an action of the
dg Lie algebra $\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$ on a complete dg module is
equivalent to an action of
$U^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})$ on the same object, and the
intertwining morphisms are identical on both sides.  Hence the
completed module categories are canonically equivalent.  Specializing
to the Yangian $\Eone$-chiral algebra gives the claimed canonical
associative dg model.
\end{proof}

\begin{conjecture}[DK-4 as tangent Lie algebra identification;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:dk4-formal-moduli}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!DK-4!formal moduli identification}
\index{dg-shifted Yangian!as tangent Lie algebra}
For the Yangian $\Eone$-chiral algebra
$\cA = \mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item The tangent Lie algebra
  $\mathfrak{g}_{\cA} = T_{*}\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$
  is quasi-isomorphic, as a filtered complete dg Lie algebra, to the
  dg-shifted Yangian $\Ydg_{\cA}$ of
  Definition~\textup{\ref{def:dg-shifted-yangian}}.
\item Under this identification, the RTT-adapted filtration
  \textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:rtt-adapted-filtration}}\textup{)}
  corresponds to the canonical filtration on
  $\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$ by order of the formal parameter: the $N$-th
  quotient $\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}/F^{N+1}$ is the tangent Lie algebra
  of the $N$-th infinitesimal neighborhood of the identity in the
  factorization group.
\item The module category equivalence
  $\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA}) \simeq
  \operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\cA)$
  is the linearization of the formal moduli problem:
  completed modules over the tangent Lie algebra classify
  infinitesimal deformations of factorization modules.
\end{enumerate}
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Relation to existing DK-4 reductions]
\label{rem:dk4-formal-moduli-vs-rtt}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!DK-4!formal moduli vs RTT}
Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk4-formal-moduli} provides a \emph{canonical}
construction of the dg-shifted Yangian, replacing the specific
RTT-adapted filtration of
Definition~\ref{def:rtt-adapted-filtration} with the universal
construction from formal moduli theory.  The two approaches are
related:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The tangent Lie algebra $\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$ exists
  unconditionally by Lurie's theorem; the content of
  Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk4-formal-moduli}(a) is that it has the
  specific algebraic structure of the dg-shifted Yangian.
\item The residue reductions of
  Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk4-typea-frontier} are
  \emph{derived} from the formal moduli identification:
  the auxiliary-kernel identity $L_a(u) = R_{0a}(u-a)$ is
  the tangent-space computation of the moduli problem
  restricted to the fundamental evaluation line.
\item The RTT-adapted filtration of
  Definition~\ref{def:rtt-adapted-filtration} is the
  \emph{coordinate expression} of the canonical formal-moduli
  filtration in the basis provided by the RTT generators.
\end{enumerate}
This reformulation clarifies the logical structure: the RTT
identities are not independent axioms but consequences of the
universal $\infty$-categorical framework applied to the specific
$\Eone$-chiral algebra~$\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$.
\end{remark}

\begin{conjecture}[DK-5 via \texorpdfstring{$\infty$}{infinity}-categorical PBW;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:dk5-infty-pbw}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!DK-5!PBW argument}
\index{PBW theorem!infinity-categorical@$\infty$-categorical}
Assume Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:dk4-formal-moduli}(a,b)}.
The full triple bridge
\textup{(}Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:full-dk-bridge}}\textup{)}
reduces to a single input: the $\infty$-categorical
Poincar\'e--Birkhoff--Witt theorem for the factorization Lie
algebra~$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item The formal group
  $G_{\cA} := \exp(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})$
  is a group object in $\Eone$-factorization coalgebras on
  $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$.  Its representation category
  $\operatorname{Rep}(G_{\cA})$ is a braided monoidal stable
  $\infty$-category.
\item The $\infty$-categorical PBW theorem gives an equivalence
  \[
  \operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})
  \;\simeq\;
  \operatorname{Rep}(G_{\cA})
  \]
  between completed modules over the Lie algebra and
  representations of the formal group.
\item If $G_{\cA} \simeq \QGspec(R_{\cA})$
  \textup{(}the spectral quantum group of
  Latyntsev~\cite{Latyntsev23}\textup{)}, then the full triple
  equivalence~\eqref{eq:triple-equivalence} follows from the chain
  \begin{multline*}
  \Factord(X;\cA)
  \;\xleftarrow[\textup{DK-3}]{\sim}\;
  \operatorname{CoFact}_{\Eone}(\cA^{!,c})^{\mathrm{op}}
  \\
  \;\xrightarrow[\textup{PBW}]{\sim}\;
  \operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})
  \;\xrightarrow[\exp]{\sim}\;
  \operatorname{Rep}(\QGspec(R_{\cA}))^{\mathrm{op}}.
  \end{multline*}
\end{enumerate}
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[The DK ladder as successive approximation to
\texorpdfstring{$\infty$}{infinity}-categorical Koszul duality]
\label{rem:unified-dk-hierarchy}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!unified hierarchy}
The five DK levels are successive approximations to $\infty$-categorical Koszul duality for $\cA = \mathcal{Y}(\fg)$:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\textbf{Level} & \textbf{Content} & \textbf{Status} \\
\hline
DK-0 & Chain-level Koszul duality on $\operatorname{Ran}_1$
  & \textbf{Proved} \\
DK-1 & Extension to $\operatorname{Ran}_n$ on evaluation objects
  & \textbf{Proved} \\
DK-2/3 & Extension to generated core (sectorwise convergence)
  & \textbf{Proved} \\
DK-4 & Tangent Lie algebra $=$ dg-shifted Yangian (Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk4-formal-moduli})
  & Conjectured \\
DK-5 & $\infty$-PBW: Lie modules $\simeq$ group representations (Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk5-infty-pbw})
  & Conjectured \\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
DK-0/1 is classical (Drinfeld--Kohno $+$ Kazhdan--Lusztig); DK-2/3 extends via Boardman convergence of the loop spectral sequence (Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}); DK-4 is the formal moduli step; DK-5 requires the exponential $\mathfrak{g}_{\cA} \to G_{\cA}$ recovering the spectral quantum group of Latyntsev~\cite{Latyntsev23}.  Contributing to Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The RTT relation as Koszul duality datum]
\label{rem:rtt-is-the-duality-datum}
\index{Yangian!RTT as Koszul datum}
\index{Koszul duality!engine of DK ladder}
The entire proved DK ladder (DK-0 through DK-3, unconditional at
all simple types) rests on a single structural observation:
\smallskip
\begin{center}
\emph{The RTT relation
$R_{12}(u\!-\!v)\,T_1(u)\,T_2(v)
= T_2(v)\,T_1(u)\,R_{12}(u\!-\!v)$
is simultaneously the defining relation of the algebra
and the input to Koszul duality.}
\end{center}

\smallskip\noindent
Three consequences, each one sentence, give the full result:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Quadratic $\Rightarrow$ $R$-matrix inversion.}
  The RTT relation is quadratic in~$T$; the orthogonal complement
  $R^\perp$ of the $R(u)$-relations is the $R^{-1}(u)$-relations,
  so $Y(\fg)^! = Y_{-\hbar}(\fg)$
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:yangian-koszul-dual}).

\item \emph{PBW $\Rightarrow$ Koszulness.}
  Molev's PBW basis gives a flat deformation to
  $\operatorname{Sym}(V)$; $\operatorname{Sym}$ is classically
  Koszul; flatness transfers Koszulness to~$Y(\fg)$, giving
  bar-cobar recovery for free
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-koszul},
  Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-bar-cobar}).

\item \emph{Root grading $\Rightarrow$ sectorwise convergence.}
  The root lattice $Q(\fg)$ decomposes the bar complex into sectors
  with $\dim V_r = (\dim V_0)^2$ uniformly; a non-increasing
  sequence of non-negative integers stabilizes; the factorization
  bar complex is therefore a genuine coalgebra on
  $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$, and K\"unneth $+$ cosheaf descent extend
  the diagonal quasi-isomorphism to all strata
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:sectorwise-spectral-convergence},
  Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}).
\end{enumerate}
These are logically independent inputs; together they give DK-2/3
for every simple~$\fg$ without any thick-generation argument.

The deeper unity: all three are consequences of the fact that
\emph{the RTT presentation expresses the Yangian as a quadratic
algebra whose defining relations encode the $R$-matrix}.
The bar construction extracts the $R$-matrix and inverts it;
PBW guarantees this extraction is lossless; the root grading
guarantees it converges sector by sector.  Geometrically:
bar-cobar duality is Verdier duality on ordered configuration
spaces, and Verdier duality reverses the orientation of ordered
collisions --- which inverts the $R$-matrix.  The RTT presentation
is, in this precise sense, the Yangian \emph{presenting itself as
a Koszul duality problem}.

For the conjectural levels: DK-4 adds no new idea.
The same PBW--Koszul--root-grading package gives surjective
transition maps $\bigwedge^n(V_{\leq N+1}^*) \twoheadrightarrow
\bigwedge^n(V_{\leq N}^*)$ on the associated graded of bar
cohomology, hence Mittag-Leffler for the RTT tower
(Theorem~\ref{thm:rtt-mittag-leffler}) and a well-behaved
completed bar-cobar equivalence
(Corollary~\ref{cor:completed-bar-cobar-yangian}).
What remains is a structure identification:
$\varprojlim_N \fg_N \cong \Ydg_\cA$
(Maurer--Cartan element, translation, coproduct).
DK-5 adds only the $\infty$-categorical PBW exponential
$\operatorname{Mod}(\fg_\cA) \simeq
\operatorname{Rep}(\exp(\fg_\cA))$.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{Coderived factorization duality off the Koszul locus}

On the Koszul locus (generic levels, evaluation-generated core),
Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd} provides an equivalence
in the ordinary derived sense.  Off the Koszul locus --- at admissible
affine levels, minimal-model central charges, or for infinite-dimensional
modules beyond the generated core --- the bar-cobar object persists as a
\emph{curved} factorization coalgebra, and the correct framework is the
coderived/contraderived category of
Positselski~\cite{Positselski11}.

\begin{theorem}[Factorization Positselski equivalence; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:factorization-positselski}
\index{Positselski!factorization equivalence|textbf}
\index{coderived category!factorization|textbf}
\index{bar-cobar duality!off the Koszul locus}
Let~$\cA$ be an $\Eone$-chiral algebra on~$X$ satisfying
hypotheses~\ref{h2:sectorwise} and~\ref{h3:convergence} of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}}
\textup{(}sectorwise finiteness and spectral convergence\textup{)},
but not necessarily~\ref{h1:koszulness}
\textup{(}$\Eone$-Koszulness\textup{)}.
Let $C = \barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA)$ denote the curved factorization
bar coalgebra.  Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The factorization coderived category
  $D^{\mathrm{co}}(C\text{-}\mathrm{CoFact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{conil}})$
  is a well-defined stable $\infty$-category: the sectorwise
  finiteness of~$C$ ensures that each $Q(\fg)$-sector is a
  genuine conilpotent coalgebra \textup{(}not a formal
  pro-object\textup{)}, so the coacyclicity localizing
  subcategory is well-defined.
\item There is a triangulated equivalence
  \begin{equation}\label{eq:factorization-positselski}
  D^{\mathrm{co}}\bigl(
    C\text{-}\mathrm{CoFact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{conil}}
  \bigr)
  \;\simeq\;
  D^{\mathrm{ctr}}\bigl(
    \cA^!\text{-}\mathrm{ContraFact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{comp}}
  \bigr),
  \end{equation}
  where the left side is the coderived category of conilpotent
  $\Eone$-factorization comodules over~$C$, and the right side is
  the contraderived category of complete \textup{(}pro-nilpotent\textup{)}
  $\Eone$-factorization contramodules over~$\cA^!$.
\item On the Koszul locus \textup{(}when~\ref{h1:koszulness}
  also holds\textup{)}, the coderived and ordinary derived categories
  coincide on compact objects, and~\eqref{eq:factorization-positselski}
  restricts to the equivalence of
  Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}(iii)}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Part~(i).}
Sectorwise finiteness (hypothesis~\ref{h2:sectorwise}) gives
$C = \bigoplus_{\gamma} C_\gamma$ with each $C_\gamma$
finite-dimensional over each $\operatorname{Ran}$-stratum.
The factorization structure on~$C$ preserves the
$Q(\fg)$-grading (Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-bar-loop-weight}(a)),
so the coaugmentation filtration
$F_0 C \subset F_1 C \subset \cdots$ has each
$F_n C_\gamma$ finite-dimensional.  The conilpotency condition
$C = \bigcup_n F_n C$ then holds sector-by-sector, and the
coacyclicity localizing subcategory (thick closure of totalizations
of exact triples, closed under coproducts) is well-defined
by the same argument as
Definition~\ref{def:chiral-coderived}, applied sectorwise.

\emph{Part~(ii).}
The chain-level comodule-contramodule correspondence
(Theorem~\ref{thm:chiral-co-contra-correspondence}) provides the
equivalence on
$\operatorname{Ran}_1(X) \cong X$.  The factorization structure
propagates this to $\operatorname{Ran}_n$ by the same
K\"unneth--descent argument as
Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}(i):
on disjoint opens the equivalence decomposes as a tensor product
of chain-level equivalences, and the factorization cosheaf
condition extends to overlapping configurations.  Sectorwise
finiteness ensures the tensor products are well-defined
(no infinite-dimensionality obstructions).

\emph{Part~(iii).}
On the Koszul locus, the curvature vanishes:
$h = m_0^{(g)} = 0$ at genus~$0$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:higher-genus-inversion}(a)).  When $h = 0$,
coacyclic = acyclic (Positselski~\cite[Thm~3.7]{Positselski11}),
so $D^{\mathrm{co}} = D^b$ on compact objects.  The restriction
of~\eqref{eq:factorization-positselski} to compacts recovers
Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}(iii).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The coderived category as the natural ambient]
\label{rem:coderived-natural-ambient}
\index{coderived category!as natural ambient for DK}
The equivalence~\eqref{eq:factorization-positselski} is the
\emph{correct categorical context} for the full MC3 programme:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item On the Koszul locus (generic level), DK-0 through DK-3
  live in the ordinary derived category, and the coderived
  category adds nothing new.  This is the domain of
  Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}.
\item Off the Koszul locus (admissible levels, minimal-model central
  charges), the bar-cobar object~$\Omega(C)$ is curved:
  $d^2 = h \neq 0$.  The ordinary derived category is trivial
  (every module is contractible via $h$), but the coderived
  category retains the full categorical information.
  The four conjectures of
  Remark~\ref{rem:corrected-mc3-frontier}(b)
  naturally live here: Baxter exact triangles, shifted-prefundamental
  generation, pro-Weyl recovery, and DK on compacts are all
  statements about the coderived/contraderived
  equivalence~\eqref{eq:factorization-positselski}.
\item The passage from the evaluation-generated core (compact objects
  in $D^b$) to the full category~$\mathcal{O}$ (possibly
  non-compact objects in $D^{\mathrm{co}}$) is controlled by the
  ind-completion of the coderived category: see
  Theorem~\ref{thm:ind-completed-extension} below.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{Ind-completed factorization extension}

The extension from the evaluation-generated core (compact objects)
to the full Yangian category~$\mathcal{O}$ (ind-completed)
is a standard categorical construction once the compact part is
established.  The key input is the
\emph{compactness of evaluation objects} in the factorization
category.

\begin{theorem}[Ind-completed factorization DK equivalence; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:ind-completed-extension}
\index{ind-completion!factorization DK|textbf}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!ind-completed extension}
Under the hypotheses of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}},
the equivalence on evaluation-generated cores extends uniquely
to an equivalence of ind-completed categories:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ind-completed-dk}
\operatorname{Ind}\bigl(
  \operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\cA)
\bigr)
\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{Ind}\bigl(
  \operatorname{CoFact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\cA^{!,c})
  ^{\mathrm{op}}
\bigr).
\end{equation}
This ind-completed category is presentable, stable, and admits
a canonical $t$-structure whose heart contains the abelian
category~$\mathcal{O}$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The evaluation-generated core
$\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\cA)$ is a small,
idempotent-complete, stable $\infty$-category
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk3-generated-core}).  The
equivalence of Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}(iii) is
an exact functor between small stable $\infty$-categories.  By
the universal property of ind-completion
(Lurie~\cite[Prop.~5.3.5.10]{HTT}), any exact equivalence between
small stable $\infty$-categories extends uniquely to a
colimit-preserving equivalence between their ind-completions.
This gives~\eqref{eq:ind-completed-dk}.

Presentability follows from $\operatorname{Ind}(\mathcal{C})$
being presentable whenever $\mathcal{C}$ is small and
idempotent-complete (Lurie~\cite[Prop.~5.5.7.8]{HTT}).
Stability is preserved by ind-completion.

The $t$-structure: evaluation objects are
bounded (finite-length in the heart of category~$\mathcal{O}$),
so they generate a bounded $t$-structure on the generated
core.  This extends to the ind-completion by
\cite[Prop.~1.3.5.21]{HA}, with heart a Grothendieck abelian
category containing~$\mathcal{O}_Y$ as a full subcategory
(via the fully faithful embedding
$\mathcal{O}_Y \hookrightarrow
\operatorname{Ind}(\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}})$
of Theorem~\ref{thm:eval-core-identification}).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Ind-completion vs.\ pro-Weyl completion]
\label{rem:ind-vs-proweyl}
\index{pro-Weyl completion!vs.\ ind-completion}
The ind-completed category
$\operatorname{Ind}(\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}})$
is the \emph{free cocompletion} of the generated core: it
formally adds all filtered colimits.  This is a strictly larger
category than the generated core but a strictly smaller one than
the full coderived category
$D^{\mathrm{co}}(\barB^{\mathrm{fact}}\text{-}\mathrm{CoFact})$
of Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-positselski}.

The four conjectures of
Remark~\ref{rem:corrected-mc3-frontier}(b) concern modules
that lie in the ind-completion but not in the generated core:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Standard modules} $M(\Psi)$: by
  Conjecture~\ref{conj:pro-weyl-recovery}, these are
  pro-Weyl limits $R\varprojlim_m W_m$, where each~$W_m$ is
  compact (evaluation-generated).  The pro-object
  $\{W_m\}$ defines an object of $\operatorname{Pro}(\mathcal{C})
  \hookrightarrow \operatorname{Ind}(\mathcal{C})$
  via the canonical functor
  $\operatorname{Pro}(\mathcal{C}) \to
  \operatorname{Ind}(\mathcal{C})^{\mathrm{op}}$.
\item \emph{Prefundamental modules} $L^-_{i,a}$: by
  Conjecture~\ref{conj:shifted-prefundamental-generation}, these
  are compact generators of the completed shifted category.
  In the ind-completed factorization category, $L^-_{i,a}$
  should be representable as a filtered colimit of evaluation
  objects (via the Baxter exact triangles of
  Conjecture~\ref{conj:baxter-exact-triangles}).
\end{enumerate}
The equivalence~\eqref{eq:ind-completed-dk} provides the
categorical framework in which both types of extensions live.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{The four conjectures in the formal moduli framework}

The formal moduli problem~$\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$
(Definition~\ref{def:factorization-formal-moduli}) provides a
unified $\infty$-categorical formulation of the four MC3
conjectures.  Each conjecture becomes a statement about the
tangent Lie algebra~$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$ or the formal
group~$G_{\cA} = \exp(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})$.

\begin{conjecture}[Formal moduli reformulation of MC3 conjectures;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:mc3-formal-moduli-reformulation}
\index{MC3!formal moduli reformulation}
\index{formal moduli problem!MC3 conjectures}
The four MC3 conjectures admit the following reformulations in terms
of the factorization formal moduli problem~$\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$
and the tangent Lie algebra
$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA} = T_{*}\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\Roman*)}]
\item \emph{Baxter
  \textup{(}Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:baxter-exact-triangles}}\textup{)}
  as infinitesimal deformation exact triangles.}
  The Baxter TQ relations lift to distinguished triangles in
  the category $\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})$
  of completed modules over the tangent Lie algebra.  The
  companion module $M_{k,x}^{(i)}$ represents the tangent
  vector to the evaluation deformation at the point
  $(k, x) \in \mathbb{C}^2$, and the TQ triangle is the
  fiber sequence of the tangent map
  $T_{(k,x)}\mathfrak{F}_{\cA} \to
  T_{(k',x')}\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$.

\item \emph{Shifted-prefundamental generation
  \textup{(}Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:shifted-prefundamental-generation}}\textup{)}
  as compact generation of the tangent category.}
  The compact objects of
  $\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})$
  are the thick closure of tangent representations at
  evaluation and prefundamental points.  In the formal moduli
  picture, these are the tangent spaces to the evaluation
  locus (compact, by the proved DK-1) and the
  prefundamental locus (conjecturally compact).

\item \emph{Pro-Weyl recovery
  \textup{(}Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:pro-weyl-recovery}}\textup{)}
  as completeness of the formal moduli problem.}
  For a rational $\ell$-weight~$\Psi$, the standard module
  $M(\Psi)$ is the derived global sections of the formal
  neighborhood of~$\Psi$ in the moduli of $\ell$-weights:
  \[
  M(\Psi)
  \;\simeq\;
  R\Gamma\bigl(\widehat{\mathrm{Spec}\,
  \mathcal{O}}_\Psi,\;
  \mathcal{V}_{\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}}\bigr)
  \;\simeq\;
  R\varprojlim_m\, W_m,
  \]
  where the Weyl modules~$W_m$ are the values of the moduli
  functor on the $m$-th infinitesimal neighborhood.

\item \emph{DK on compacts
  \textup{(}Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:dk-compacts-completion}}\textup{)}
  as formal GAGA.}
  The bar-cobar equivalence extends from the generic
  fiber (evaluation locus) to the formal neighborhood
  (completed category) by a formal GAGA principle for
  the factorization formal moduli problem:
  coherent sheaves on the formal completion agree with
  algebraic coherent sheaves on the Koszul locus.
\end{enumerate}
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Tangent Lie algebra controls the extension programme]
\label{rem:tangent-controls-extension}
\index{tangent Lie algebra!role in MC3 extension}
The formal moduli reformulation
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:mc3-formal-moduli-reformulation})
reveals the organizing role of the tangent Lie
algebra~$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$: all four MC3 extension
conjectures are consequences of a single structural property of
$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$, namely that it is \emph{algebraizable} ---
that the formal moduli problem~$\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$ is the
formal completion of a global (algebraic) moduli problem.

In the DK-4 framework
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk4-formal-moduli}), algebraizability is the
content of the RTT-adapted filtration: the formal
group~$G_{\cA}$ admits a filtration whose finite quotients are
the finite RTT stages, and the transition maps are the RTT
truncations.  If this filtration is Mittag-Leffler on cohomology
(the concrete form of algebraizability), all four conjectures
follow by the MC4 reduction principle
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:inverse-limit-completed-bar-cobar}).

This reduces the four MC3 conjectures to a single input:
\emph{the Mittag-Leffler property of the RTT tower on bar
cohomology.}
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{Factorization DK-4: tangent Lie algebra via
bar derivations}

Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk4-formal-moduli} identifies DK-4 with the
tangent Lie algebra computation
$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA} \simeq \Ydg_{\cA}$.
The following proposition provides the first constructive step:
the tangent Lie algebra at finite RTT stage is computable,
and the compatibility of these finite computations is the
content of DK-4.

\begin{proposition}[Finite-stage tangent Lie algebras;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:finite-stage-tangent}
\index{tangent Lie algebra!finite RTT stage}
\index{dg-shifted Yangian!finite-stage construction}
For the Yangian $\Eone$-chiral algebra
$\cA = \mathcal{Y}(\fg)$ and the $N$-th RTT truncation
$\cA_{\leq N}$, the tangent Lie algebra
$\mathfrak{g}_N := T_{*}\mathfrak{F}_{\cA_{\leq N}}$
satisfies:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item $\mathfrak{g}_N$ is a finite-dimensional dg Lie algebra
  with $N \cdot (\dim V_0)^2$ generators in degree~$0$
  \textup{(}one copy of $\operatorname{End}(V_0)$ per RTT
  level; for the reduced Yangian, $N \cdot \dim \fg$
  generators\textup{)}.
\item The differential on~$\mathfrak{g}_N$ is the derivation
  of $\barB(\cA_{\leq N})$ induced by the bar differential:
  \[
  \mathfrak{g}_N
  \;\cong\;
  \operatorname{Der}^{\mathrm{cont}}\bigl(
    \barB(\cA_{\leq N}),\, \barB(\cA_{\leq N})
  \bigr)[1].
  \]
\item The truncation maps $\cA_{\leq N+1} \to \cA_{\leq N}$
  induce surjective dg Lie algebra maps
  $\mathfrak{g}_{N+1} \twoheadrightarrow \mathfrak{g}_N$,
  compatible with the bar construction.
\item At $N = 1$, $\mathfrak{g}_1 \cong \mathfrak{gl}(V_0)$
  \textup{(}the RTT generators $T_{ij}^{(0)}$ at level~$0$ span
  $\operatorname{End}(V_0)$ with the commutator bracket\textup{)},
  concentrated in degree~$0$.  For the reduced Yangian
  $Y(\fg)$ \textup{(}quantum determinant quotient\textup{)},
  $\mathfrak{g}_1 \cong \fg$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Part~(a):
$\cA_{\leq N}$ is the quotient of~$\cA$ by generators of
level $> N$.  Each level contributes $(\dim V_0)^2$
generators (the RTT modes $T_{ij}^{(r)}$ for
$0 \leq r \leq N-1$), so $\mathfrak{g}_N$ has
$N \cdot (\dim V_0)^2$ generators in degree~$0$.
Since $\cA_{\leq N}$ is quadratic and Koszul
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-koszul}), the tangent Lie
algebra $\mathfrak{g}_N \cong
\operatorname{Ext}^*_{\cA_{\leq N}}(\bC, \bC)[1]$ is
finite-dimensional (each degree of the Koszul dual
$\cA_{\leq N}^!$ is finite-dimensional by local finiteness).

Part~(b):
By Lurie's formal moduli theorem~\cite{LurieDAGX}, the tangent
Lie algebra is computed as the shifted derivations of the bar
coalgebra.  For the finite-dimensional quotient~$\cA_{\leq N}$,
the bar coalgebra $\barB(\cA_{\leq N})$ is finite-dimensional
(bounded bar degree by the quadratic relations), so
the derivation complex is finite-dimensional.

Part~(c):
The truncation map $\cA_{\leq N+1} \twoheadrightarrow \cA_{\leq N}$
induces a surjection
$\barB(\cA_{\leq N+1}) \twoheadrightarrow \barB(\cA_{\leq N})$
of bar coalgebras (bar is covariant on algebra maps).

For the tangent Lie algebras, the map
$\mathfrak{g}_{N+1} \to \mathfrak{g}_N$ is surjective by the
following Koszul dual argument: since $\cA_{\leq N}$ is Koszul,
the tangent Lie algebra in degree~$p$ is
$(\mathfrak{g}_N)_p \cong (\cA_{\leq N}^!)_{p+1}$.

The Koszul dual $\cA_{\leq N}^!$ has generators
$V_{\leq N}^*$ and relations $R_{\leq N}^\perp$.
Any element $f \in (\cA_{\leq N}^!)_n
\subset (V_{\leq N}^*)^{\otimes n} \cap (R_{\leq N}^\perp)_n$
extends by zero on the $V_N^*$-components to an element
$\tilde{f} \in (\cA_{\leq N+1}^!)_n$
(since $\tilde{f}$ automatically annihilates all
relations involving level-$N$ generators).
Hence $(\cA_{\leq N+1}^!)_n \twoheadrightarrow (\cA_{\leq N}^!)_n$
is surjective in every degree.

The identification
$(\mathfrak{g}_N)_p \cong (\cA_{\leq N}^!)_{p+1}$ is natural
in~$N$: it arises from Lurie's formal moduli theorem (Part~(b))
applied to each truncation, and the truncation-compatible maps of
bar coalgebras induce compatible maps on derivation complexes.
Thus the surjectivity of $(\cA_{\leq N+1}^!)_n \twoheadrightarrow
(\cA_{\leq N}^!)_n$ directly yields
$\mathfrak{g}_{N+1} \twoheadrightarrow \mathfrak{g}_N$ in every
internal degree.

Part~(d):
At $N = 1$, $\cA_{\leq 1} \cong U(\mathfrak{gl}(V_0))$ (the
$T_{ij}^{(0)}$ for $1 \leq i,j \leq \dim V_0$ generate
$\operatorname{End}(V_0) = \mathfrak{gl}(V_0)$ under the
commutator, and the RTT relation at level~$0$ reproduces the
$\mathfrak{gl}(V_0)$ bracket).  The bar complex
$\barB(U(\mathfrak{gl}(V_0)))$ is the Chevalley--Eilenberg complex,
and $\operatorname{Der}(\barB(U(\mathfrak{gl}(V_0))))[1]
\cong \mathfrak{gl}(V_0)$, concentrated in degree~$0$.
The quantum determinant condition at level~$0$ reduces the
identity component, giving $\mathfrak{g}_1 \cong \fg$ for
the reduced Yangian.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Mittag-Leffler for the RTT bar cohomology tower;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:rtt-mittag-leffler}
\index{Mittag-Leffler condition!RTT tower|textbf}
\index{bar complex!RTT tower!Mittag-Leffler}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!DK-4!Mittag-Leffler}
For any simple Lie algebra~$\fg$, the transition maps on bar
cohomology in the RTT tower are surjective:
\[
H^n\bigl(\barB(\cA_{\leq N+1})\bigr)
\;\twoheadrightarrow\;
H^n\bigl(\barB(\cA_{\leq N})\bigr)
\qquad \text{for all } N \geq 1, \;\text{all } n \geq 0.
\]
In particular, the Mittag-Leffler condition holds and
$\varprojlim^1_N H^n(\barB(\cA_{\leq N})) = 0$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step~1: PBW filtration on truncated bar complexes.}
Each truncation $\cA_{\leq N} = Y(\fg)_{\leq N}$ inherits the
PBW filtration of Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-koszul}:
$F_p \cA_{\leq N}$ is spanned by ordered monomials of total
level $\leq p$ in the RTT generators $\{T_{ij}^{(r)}\}_{r < N}$.
The associated graded is the polynomial algebra:
\[
\operatorname{gr}_F \cA_{\leq N}
\;\cong\;
\operatorname{Sym}(V_{\leq N}),
\qquad
V_{\leq N} = \bigoplus_{r=0}^{N-1}
\operatorname{End}(\bC^{N_0})_r,
\]
where $N_0 = \dim V_0$.  The truncation maps
$\cA_{\leq N+1} \twoheadrightarrow \cA_{\leq N}$ preserve the
PBW filtration and induce the projection
$\operatorname{Sym}(V_{\leq N+1}) \twoheadrightarrow
\operatorname{Sym}(V_{\leq N})$ on associated graded.

\emph{Step~2: PBW spectral sequence for bar cohomology.}
The PBW filtration induces a bounded-below, exhaustive filtration
on $\barB(\cA_{\leq N})$.  By
Theorem~\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion} (``bar construction
commutes with taking associated graded for flat filtrations''),
the associated spectral sequence has $E_1$ page
\[
E_1^{p,q}(\cA_{\leq N})
= H^{p+q}\bigl(\barB(\operatorname{Sym}(V_{\leq N}))\bigr).
\]
By Koszulness of $\cA_{\leq N}$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-koszul} applies to each truncation:
$\cA_{\leq N}$ is a quadratic algebra in finitely many generators
$\{T_{ij}^{(r)}\}_{r < N}$ with the restricted RTT relations, inherits
the PBW basis of Molev, and satisfies local finiteness a~fortiori),
the spectral sequence \emph{degenerates at $E_1$}:
$E_1 = E_\infty$.  Indeed, Koszulness forces bar cohomology
onto the diagonal $p + q = n$, $p = n$ (homological = internal
degree), so all higher differentials $d_r$ for $r \geq 2$ have
zero source or target for bidegree reasons.

\emph{Step~3: Surjectivity on $E_1$.}
For the commutative algebra $\operatorname{Sym}(V_{\leq N})$,
the Koszul dual is $\bigwedge(V_{\leq N}^*)$, and bar cohomology
in degree~$n$ is $\bigwedge^n(V_{\leq N}^*)$.  The truncation
$\operatorname{Sym}(V_{\leq N+1}) \twoheadrightarrow
\operatorname{Sym}(V_{\leq N})$ induces on bar cohomology the
projection
\[
\textstyle
\bigwedge\nolimits^n(V_{\leq N+1}^*)
\;\twoheadrightarrow\;
\bigwedge\nolimits^n(V_{\leq N}^*),
\]
which kills exactly the wedge products involving the factor
$\operatorname{End}(\bC^{N_0})_N^*$.  This map is surjective
for all $N$ and $n$.

\emph{Step~4: Filtered surjectivity implies surjectivity.}
The truncation maps $\cA_{\leq N+1} \to \cA_{\leq N}$ are
compatible with the PBW filtrations, hence induce a map of
spectral sequences.  On the $E_1 = E_\infty$ page, this map
is the surjection of Step~3.  Since the PBW filtration on
$H^n(\barB(\cA_{\leq N}))$ is exhaustive and bounded below
(each bar degree and level contributes finitely), a standard
filtered-surjectivity argument gives: a filtered map
$f\colon M' \to M$ of filtered objects inducing a surjection
$\operatorname{gr}_p f$ on each graded piece is itself
surjective.  (Proof: by induction on $p$, the image of
$f$ contains $F_p M$ for each~$p$; exhaustivity gives
$\operatorname{im}(f) = M$.)

Therefore $H^n(\barB(\cA_{\leq N+1}))
\twoheadrightarrow H^n(\barB(\cA_{\leq N}))$
is surjective for all $N$ and~$n$.  Surjective transition maps
trivially satisfy Mittag-Leffler, giving
$\varprojlim^1 = 0$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Completed bar-cobar equivalence for Yangians;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:completed-bar-cobar-yangian}
\index{bar-cobar duality!completed Yangian|textbf}
\index{Yangian!completed bar-cobar}
For any simple~$\fg$, the completed reduced bar construction
\[
\widehat{\barB}\bigl(Y(\fg)\bigr)
\;:=\;
\varprojlim_N\, \barB\bigl(Y(\fg)_{\leq N}\bigr)
\]
exists as a separated complete conilpotent $\Eone$-chiral coalgebra,
and the completed cobar-bar counit is a quasi-isomorphism:
\[
\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}\bigl(
  \widehat{\barB}(Y(\fg))
\bigr)
\;\xrightarrow{\;\sim\;}\;
Y(\fg).
\]
This resolves
Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:inverse-limit-completed-bar-cobar}}
for the Yangian RTT tower.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The three hypotheses of
Conjecture~\ref{conj:inverse-limit-completed-bar-cobar} are verified:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item Each truncation $\cA_{\leq N}$ is finite type and lies in
  the proved bar-cobar regime
  (Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-bar-cobar}).
\item The transition maps $\cA_{\leq N+1} \to \cA_{\leq N}$ are
  compatible with the finite-stage bar constructions
  (PBW filtration compatibility,
  Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-stage-tangent}(c)).
\item The inverse system on bar complexes satisfies Mittag-Leffler
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:rtt-mittag-leffler}): the transition maps
  on bar cohomology are surjective, so
  $\varprojlim^1_N H^n(\barB(\cA_{\leq N})) = 0$.
\end{enumerate}
The Mittag-Leffler condition gives
$H^n(\widehat{\barB}(Y(\fg)))
\cong \varprojlim_N H^n(\barB(\cA_{\leq N}))$
(no $\varprojlim^1$ correction).  The completed cobar differential
is continuous by
Proposition~\ref{prop:inverse-limit-differential-continuity}
(automatic for inverse systems of finite-stage curved dg
coalgebras).  By the MC4 reduction principle
(Proposition~\ref{prop:mc4-reduction-principle},
now verified for this tower), the completed cobar-bar counit
restricts at each finite stage to the proved
quasi-isomorphism
$\Omega(\barB(\cA_{\leq N})) \xrightarrow{\sim} \cA_{\leq N}$,
and the Mittag-Leffler condition ensures the inverse limit
of quasi-isomorphisms is a quasi-isomorphism.
\end{proof}

\begin{conjecture}[DK-4: tangent Lie algebra identification;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:dk4-inverse-limit}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!DK-4!inverse limit construction}
\index{tangent Lie algebra!inverse limit}
By Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:rtt-mittag-leffler}}, the
inverse system $\{\mathfrak{g}_N\}_{N \geq 1}$ of
Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:finite-stage-tangent}} satisfies
Mittag-Leffler with surjective transition maps, and the tangent
Lie algebra of the factorization formal moduli problem is
\[
\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}
\;=\;
T_{*}\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}
\;\cong\;
\varprojlim_N\, \mathfrak{g}_N.
\]
The remaining content of DK-4 is the identification of this
inverse limit with the dg-shifted Yangian:
\[
\varprojlim_N\, \mathfrak{g}_N
\;\cong\;
\Ydg_{\cA}.
\]
This identification is equivalent to showing that the derivation
complex $\operatorname{Der}(\widehat{\barB}(Y(\fg)))$
carries the dg-shifted RTT structure
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:dg-shifted-yangian}}\textup{)}:
the Maurer--Cartan element $r(z) = \tau|_{\deg 2}$, the
translation operator, and the twisted coproduct.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[DK-4 reduced to structure identification]
\label{rem:dk4-mittag-leffler}
\index{Mittag-Leffler condition!DK-4 reduction}
Theorem~\ref{thm:rtt-mittag-leffler} and
Corollary~\ref{cor:completed-bar-cobar-yangian} resolve the
\emph{analytic} part of DK-4: the inverse limit exists, is
well-behaved ($\varprojlim^1 = 0$), and the completed bar-cobar
equivalence holds.  What remains is the \emph{algebraic}
identification of $\varprojlim_N \mathfrak{g}_N$ with the
dg-shifted Yangian --- specifically, the three structural
data:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item the Maurer--Cartan element $r(z)$ arises as the
  degree-$2$ part of the bar propagator~$\tau$;
\item the translation operator is the derivation induced by
  $T_{ij}^{(r)} \mapsto T_{ij}^{(r+1)}$;
\item the twisted coproduct on $\widehat{\barB}(Y(\fg))$
  decomposes as the Drinfeld coproduct on~$\Ydg$.
\end{enumerate}
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk4-typea-frontier} verifies
(a) at finite stages via the auxiliary-kernel identity
$L_a(u) = R_{0a}(u - a)$, which is the tangent-space
computation of the moduli problem restricted to the
fundamental evaluation line
(Remark~\ref{rem:dk4-formal-moduli-vs-rtt}(ii)).

The completed bar-cobar equivalence
(Corollary~\ref{cor:completed-bar-cobar-yangian}) also sharpens
the four MC3 extension conjectures
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:mc3-formal-moduli-reformulation}):
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Pro-Weyl recovery}
  \textup{(}Conjecture~\ref{conj:pro-weyl-recovery}\textup{)}:
  for each rational $\ell$-weight~$\Psi$ with Drinfeld
  polynomial of degree~$d$, the Weyl module $W_m$ for
  $m \geq d$ is a module over~$\cA_{\leq m}$, and
  the transition maps $W_{m+1} \twoheadrightarrow W_m$ are
  surjective (universal highest-weight quotients).
  The completed bar-cobar equivalence transports the
  pro-Weyl system to a pro-system of bar complexes
  satisfying Mittag-Leffler, giving
  $M(\Psi) \simeq \varprojlim_m W_m$ in the completed
  factorization category.

\item \emph{DK on compacts}
  \textup{(}Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk-compacts-completion}\textup{)}:
  the Francis--Gaitsgory pro-nilpotent completion of the
  evaluation-generated core is now a quotient of the
  ind-completed category
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:ind-completed-extension}), with the
  completed bar-cobar equivalence providing the passage.
  What remains is the compact generation statement of
  Conjecture~\ref{conj:shifted-prefundamental-generation}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Ordered \texorpdfstring{$\Eone$}{E1}-factorization category]
\label{def:ordered-e1-factorization}
\index{factorization category!ordered $\Eone$-|textbf}
For an $\Eone$-chiral algebra~$\cA$ on a curve~$X$,
the \emph{ordered $\Eone$-factorization category}
$\Factord(X;\cA)$ is the stable $\infty$-category
of $\cA$-modules on ordered configuration spaces,
with the associative chiral tensor structure induced
by the $\Eone$-operad action
(Definition~\ref{def:e1-factorization-category}).
(Contributing to Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.)
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Spectral quantum group]
\label{def:spectral-quantum-group}
\index{quantum group!spectral|textbf}
For a Koszul dual~$\cA^!$ with spectral $R$-matrix~$R_{\cA}$,
the \emph{spectral quantum group} $\QGspec(R_{\cA})$ is the
factorization quantum group whose representation category
is controlled by the spectral $R$-matrix, in the sense of
Latyntsev~\cite{Latyntsev23}.
(Contributing to Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.)
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[dg-shifted Yangian]
\label{def:dg-shifted-yangian}
\index{Yangian!dg-shifted|textbf}
For a Koszul dual~$\cA^!$, the \emph{dg-shifted Yangian}
$\Ydg_{\cA}$ is the dg algebra with translation operator,
Maurer--Cartan element~$r(z)$, and twisted coproduct,
as constructed in the perturbative holomorphic-topological
setting of Costello--Yamazaki~\cite{costello-yamazaki} and
Costello--Gwilliam~\cite{CG17}.
(Contributing to Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.)
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[RTT-adapted filtration on a dg-shifted Yangian]
\label{def:rtt-adapted-filtration}
Let $\Ydg_{\cA}$ be a dg-shifted Yangian.  An
\emph{RTT-adapted filtration} on $\Ydg_{\cA}$ is a descending
filtration by closed dg ideals
\[
F^1\Ydg_{\cA} \supset F^2\Ydg_{\cA} \supset \cdots
\]
such that:
\begin{enumerate}
\item $\Ydg_{\cA} \cong
  \varprojlim_N \Ydg_{\cA}/F^{N+1}\Ydg_{\cA}$ as a complete dg algebra;
\item the differential, translation operator, Maurer--Cartan element
  $r(z)$, and twisted coproduct preserve the filtration;
\item each quotient
  $\Ydg_{\cA}/F^{N+1}\Ydg_{\cA}$ is dg quasi-isomorphic to the finite
  RTT stage $Y_{\le N}$; and
\item these quotient quasi-isomorphisms are compatible with the RTT
  truncation maps and the finite-stage bar-cobar data.
\end{enumerate}
This is the exact H-level input required by
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-hlevel-comparison-criterion}.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Formal quotient criterion for dg-shifted Yangians;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:dg-shifted-quotient-criterion}
Let $\Ydg_{\cA}$ be a dg algebra equipped with:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a translation operator;
\item a Maurer--Cartan element $r(z)$;
\item a twisted coproduct; and
\item a descending sequence of closed dg ideals
  \[
  F^1\Ydg_{\cA} \supset F^2\Ydg_{\cA} \supset \cdots
  \]
  preserved by the differential, translation operator,
  Maurer--Cartan element, and twisted coproduct.
\end{enumerate}
Then every finite quotient
\[
\Ydg_{\cA}/F^{N+1}\Ydg_{\cA}
\]
inherits the same dg-shifted Yangian type of structure, and the quotient
maps form an inverse system of dg-shifted objects.

If, in addition, these quotients are dg quasi-isomorphic to the finite
RTT stages $Y_{\le N}$ compatibly with RTT truncation, evaluation
modules, and the degree-$2$ twisting morphism, then
Definition~\ref{def:rtt-adapted-filtration} holds and
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-hlevel-comparison-criterion} applies.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Preservation of the ideals by the differential descends the dg
structure to each quotient.  Preservation by the translation operator,
Maurer--Cartan element, and twisted coproduct descends those data as
well, because each operation factors through the quotient by the same
ideal.  Compatibility of the quotient maps with the preserved
operations makes the family of quotients an inverse system of
dg-shifted objects.

The additional compatibility hypotheses are exactly the remaining items
of Definition~\ref{def:rtt-adapted-filtration}.  Once they are checked,
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-hlevel-comparison-criterion} gives the
comparison with $\widehat Y_{\mathrm{RTT}}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{conjecture}[Full derived Drinfeld--Kohno bridge;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:full-dk-bridge}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!full bridge|textbf}
\index{triple equivalence!factorization--Yangian--quantum group}
For affine/Yangian-type modular Koszul $\Eone$-objects~$\cA$
satisfying:
\textup{(i)}~$\Eone$-Koszulness,
\textup{(ii)}~pro-nilpotent completion/convergence,
\textup{(iii)}~existence of spectral $R$-matrix data, and
\textup{(iv)}~extension of the evaluation-locus comparison to
the full category~$\mathcal{O}$,
there are equivalences of braided monoidal stable
$\infty$-categories
\begin{equation}\label{eq:triple-equivalence}
\Factord(X;\cA)
\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA})
\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}\!
  \bigl(\QGspec(R_{\cA})\bigr)^{\mathrm{op}},
\end{equation}
compatible with evaluation modules and KZ/KZB monodromy,
and identifying $r(z) = \tau|_{\deg 2}$ where $\tau$ is
the propagator of the $\Eone$-bar complex.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Status.}
Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:full-derived-dk}} is the DK-3 outer
factorization equivalence; Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}}
proves DK-1 on the evaluation locus.  The Yangian middle term and the
triple formulation are the DK-4/DK-5 completion.
(Contributing to Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.)
\end{conjecture}

\begin{proposition}[Formal reduction principle from DK-3 to
DK-4/DK-5; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk-mc4-reduction}
Fix an affine/Yangian-type modular Koszul $\Eone$-object~$\cA$.
Assume the DK-3 outer equivalence is established on the ordered
factorization model, namely that there is a braided monoidal
equivalence
\[
\Factord(X;\cA)
\xrightarrow{\sim}
\operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}\!
  \bigl(\QGspec(R_{\cA})\bigr)^{\mathrm{op}}
\]
compatible with evaluation modules and extending the
evaluation-locus comparison of
Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}.  Then the remaining content of
Conjecture~\ref{conj:full-dk-bridge} is exactly the construction of a
dg-shifted Yangian~$\Ydg_{\cA}$ whose RTT-adapted filtration satisfies
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-hlevel-comparison-criterion}, together with
the module-category enhancement
\[
\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA})
\xrightarrow{\sim}
\operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}\!
  \bigl(\QGspec(R_{\cA})\bigr)^{\mathrm{op}}.
\]
In particular, once DK-3 is in hand, the genuinely new Yangian input is
the MC4 H-level comparison problem and its passage from completed
dg-algebra comparison to completed module-category equivalence; it is
not a second factorization comparison on the evaluation locus.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The ordered factorization term and the right-hand spectral quantum-group
term in~\eqref{eq:triple-equivalence} are fixed by the assumed DK-3
outer equivalence, so after DK-3 the only missing part of
Conjecture~\ref{conj:full-dk-bridge} is the middle equivalence
\[
\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA})
\simeq
\operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}\!
  \bigl(\QGspec(R_{\cA})\bigr)^{\mathrm{op}}.
\]
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-hlevel-comparison-criterion} shows that, once
$\Ydg_{\cA}$ carries a separated complete RTT-adapted filtration with
the theorematic finite RTT quotients, the underlying completed dg
algebra comparison with the standard RTT completion becomes formal.
Thus the remaining mathematical content is precisely the MC4
construction of that filtered H-level target together with the passage
from the dg comparison to the completed module-category equivalence
displayed above.  This is exactly the DK-4/DK-5 remainder.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[DK-4 reduction to the fundamental residue packet in
standard type~A; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk4-typea-frontier}
Assume the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk-mc4-reduction} and work with the
standard type-A RTT tower.  Then the remaining DK-4 input is reduced to
the boundary-strip identities
\[
\Delta_{a,0}(N)=0
\qquad (0\le a\le N,\ N\ge 0)
\]
for the defects
\[
\Delta_{a,0}(N)
=\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{line}}_{a,0}(N)
-\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{RTT}}_{a,0}(N),
\]
together with the standard twisted-coproduct multiplication law on
fundamental evaluation modules.  Equivalently, for the standard type-A
tower it is enough to prove the pairwise auxiliary-kernel identity
\[
L_a(u)=R_{0a}(u-a)
\]
on the fundamental evaluation line.

If, moreover, the one-factor line operator is functorial for the
diagonal $\mathfrak{sl}_M$-action and normalized by
$L_a(u)\to 1$ as $u\to\infty$, then the same DK-4 input is further
reduced to transport of the standard residue formula
\[
\operatorname*{Res}_{u=a}L_a(u)=-\hbar P.
\]
For $M\ge 2$, this transport statement is further reduced to the
ordered mixed-tensor
identity
\[
\Xi_a(e_1\otimes e_2)=-\hbar(e_2\otimes e_1).
\]

By
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-uniform-single-line},
this single ordered tensor-line computation already determines the full
residue operator $\Xi_a=-\hbar P$ uniformly in the rank.
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-standard-typea-local-packet}
shows that this residue formula already holds on the theorematic
standard RTT tower itself.  Thus the genuinely live local input is to
identify the dg-shifted or factorization one-factor kernel with that
standard normalized residue, equivalently with the same mixed-tensor
matrix coefficient on the fundamental line.

Under one-loop exactness,
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-degree2-mixed-tensor-criterion}
reduces this transport problem further to the ordered mixed-tensor
coefficient of the degree-$2$ twisting morphism $r(z)=\tau|_{\deg 2}$.
Corollary~\ref{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-seed-normalized-coefficient}
shows that, in the standard logarithmic normalization, this is
equivalently the ordered mixed-tensor coefficient of the operator
$r_a^{\mathrm{fund}}(z)$ itself.

Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-degree2-scalar-normalization}
then removes the remaining one-loop matrix ambiguity: after
degree-$2$ scalar normalization, the only genuinely live datum is the
scalar coefficient of the permutation operator.  In particular,
Corollary~\ref{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-degree2-casimir-normalization}
shows that the trace-zero convention
$P-\frac{1}{M}\id$ reduces to the same scalar packet, and
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-degree2-fundamental-casimir}
computes that scalar as $-1$ once the standard fundamental Casimir
insertion is identified.
Corollary~\ref{cor:factorization-fundamental-casimir-identity} proves
that the factorization side already satisfies this identity, and
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-factorization-shared-seed} shows that
any dg-shifted realization presented by the same ordered bar seed
inherits the same coefficient.  Thus the genuinely live local step is
no longer a new coefficient computation, but the realization of the
dg-shifted target with that shared bar seed.

Thus, after DK-3, the genuinely analytic Yangian frontier on the
standard type-A tower is the H-level dg-shifted realization and the
compact-core DK-5 packet, not a new residue computation inside the
standard RTT tower.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk-mc4-reduction}, once DK-3 is fixed
the remaining work is to construct a dg-shifted Yangian with an
RTT-adapted filtration satisfying
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-hlevel-comparison-criterion}.  The finite
quotient comparison required there is reduced by
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-oneloop-kernel-criterion} to the
coefficient identities
$\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{line}}_{a,b}(N)
=\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{RTT}}_{a,b}(N)$,
by Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-boundary-seed} to the boundary
strip $\Delta_{a,0}(N)$, and by
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-fundamental-propagation} to the
fundamental evaluation family together with the standard
twisted-coproduct multiplication law.

Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-auxiliary-kernel-criterion} then
reduces this boundary-strip packet to the pairwise kernel identity
$L_a(u)=R_{0a}(u-a)$ on the fundamental line.  Under the symmetry and
normalization hypotheses,
Corollary~\ref{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-residue-reduction} reduces that
identity to the residue formula
$\operatorname*{Res}_{u=a}L_a(u)=-\hbar P$, and
Corollary~\ref{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-single-line} reduces the
transport-normalized residue formula further to the ordered
mixed-tensor check displayed in
the statement, while
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-uniform-single-line}
shows that this one check already determines the whole residue
operator uniformly in~$M$.  Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-standard-typea-local-packet}
then identifies that residue explicitly on the theorematic standard
RTT side.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[DK-5 reduction to compact-generator comparison;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk5-compact-generators}
Assume the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk4-typea-frontier}.  Let
\[
\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{Y}
\subset \operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA}),
\qquad
\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}
\subset \operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}\!
  \bigl(\QGspec(R_{\cA})\bigr)^{\mathrm{op}}
\]
be the full subcategories generated by the completed images of finite
ordered tensor products of fundamental evaluation modules.  Assume:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item both ambient stable categories are compactly generated, and
  their compact objects are the thick idempotent-complete closures of
  $\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{Y}$ and
  $\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}$, respectively;
\item the DK-4 comparison supplies an exact colimit-preserving functor
  \[
  F_{\mathrm{comp}}\colon
  \operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA})
  \longrightarrow
  \operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}\!
    \bigl(\QGspec(R_{\cA})\bigr)^{\mathrm{op}}
  \]
  compatible with the dg comparison
  $\Ydg_{\cA}\xrightarrow{\sim}\widehat Y_{\mathrm{RTT}}$ and with the
  DK-3 transport on the evaluation-generated packet; and
\item the restriction of $F_{\mathrm{comp}}$ to
  $\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{Y}$ is an equivalence onto
  $\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}$.
\end{enumerate}
Then $F_{\mathrm{comp}}$ is an equivalence of stable categories.  In
particular, after DK-4 the remaining DK-5 input is the compact-generator
comparison on the completed module categories; the passage from that
packet to the full completed equivalence is formal.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By assumption~\textup{(iii)}, the functor
$F_{\mathrm{comp}}$ is an equivalence on the chosen generator packet.
Because $F_{\mathrm{comp}}$ is exact, it preserves shifts, cones, and
direct summands, so it is an equivalence on the thick idempotent-complete
closures of that packet.  Assumption~\textup{(i)} identifies those
closures with the compact objects in the two ambient categories.

Now both categories are compactly generated, and
$F_{\mathrm{comp}}$ preserves colimits by assumption~\textup{(ii)}.
Hence the same uniqueness-of-extension mechanism used in the proof of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chiral-co-contra-correspondence} applies: an exact
colimit-preserving functor between compactly generated stable
categories is determined by its restriction to compact generators, and
an equivalence on those generators extends to an equivalence on the
whole categories.  Therefore $F_{\mathrm{comp}}$ is an equivalence.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Compact-core comparison reduces to the completed
fundamental packet; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk5-fundamental-packet}
Work in the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-compact-generators}.  Write
\[
\mathcal{C}_Y^\omega
:=
\operatorname{thick}^{\mathrm{idemp}}
\bigl(\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{Y}\bigr),
\qquad
